Taken together, these results demonstrate that tebentafusp induced a broad and potent anti-tumor 
immune response in metastatic uveal melanoma patients enrolled in the Phase 2 trial and support 
the proposed mechanism of action for tebentafusp.

The Applicant’s Position:

The mechanism of action and pharmacodynamic effects of tebentafusp were explored in the 
Phase 1 (Study IMCgp100-01, primarily cutaneous melanoma) and Phase 2 trials (Study 
IMCgp100-102). The analysis below is focused on Study IMCgp100-102 because it enrolled

#### IFN

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

70 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

uveal melanoma patients who were treated at the 68 mcg dose after IE dose escalation, a regimen 
that was identical to that used in the Phase 3 study IMCgp100-202. Similar trends were observed 
in the Phase 1 trial (Middleton et al., 2020). The key pharmacodynamic effects of tebentafusp 
observed in study IMCgp100-102 are summarized here:

 Tebentafusp induced transient reductions in blood lymphocyte levels which were 
accompanied by transient increases in serum inflammatory cytokines and 
chemokines.

 Tebentafusp increased CD3, CD4 and CD8 T cells levels in the tumor, consistent 
with T cell trafficking into the tumor microenvironment.

 Tebentafusp induced Type 1 (IFNα) and Type 2 (IFNγ) interferon pathways in 
tumors.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
FDA considers the above biomarker assessments as supportive information to understand 
tebentafusp’s mechanism of action.

## Clinical Pharmacology Questions

6.3.2.1 Does the clinical pharmacology program provide supportive evidence of 
effectiveness? 
Data:

#### See General Pharmacology and Pharmacokinetic Characteristics Above

The Applicant’s Position:

Yes, the mechanism of action and pharmacodynamic effects of tebentafusp were explored in the 
Phase 1 (Study IMCgp100-01, primarily cutaneous melanoma) and Phase 2 trials (Study 
IMCgp100-102). The analysis below is focused on Study IMCgp100-102 because it enrolled 
uveal melanoma patients who were treated at the 68 mcg dose after IE dose escalation, a regimen 
that was identical to that used in the Phase 3 study IMCgp100-202. Similar trends were observed 
in the Phase 1 trial (Middleton et al., 2020). The key pharmacodynamic effects of tebentafusp 
observed in study IMCgp100-102 are summarized here:

 Tebentafusp induced transient reductions in blood lymphocyte levels which were 
accompanied by transient increases in serum inflammatory cytokines and 
chemokines.

 Tebentafusp increased CD3, CD4 and CD8 T cells levels in the tumor, consistent 
with T cell trafficking into the tumor microenvironment.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
|  |
| FDA considers the above biomarker assessments as supportive information to understand |
| tebentafusp’s mechanism of action. |

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

71 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews)

Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

 Tebentafusp induced Type 1 (IFNα) and Type 2 (IFNγ) interferon pathways in 
tumors.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
FDA considers the above assessments of tebentafusp pharmacodynamic effects as supportive 
information to understand tebentafusp’s mechanism of action.

Is the proposed dosing regimen appropriate for the general patient 
population for which the indication is being sought?

Data: 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

Justification for the Phase 3 tebentafusp dose and regimen is based on clinical data driven by 
safety, tolerability, and clinical activity from the dose escalation phases of study IMCgp100-01 
and study IMCgp100-102 with supporting data from the expansion phase of study 
IMCgp100-102 rather than tebentafusp exposure-response. Validation of the tebentafusp regimen 
is provided by the Phase 3 results, including high OS (Hazard Ratio 0.51 for OS) and overall 
tolerability (low rate of tebentafusp-related discontinuations [3.1% Phase 2, 2.0% Phase 3] and 
no tebentafusp-related deaths).

The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s position that the proposed dosing regimen of tebentafusp for 
the general patient population (20 mcg on Day 1, 30 mcg on Day 8, 68 mcg on Day 15, and 68 
mcg once every week thereafter ) is selected based on safety, tolerability and clinical activity 
from study IMCgp100‐01 and study IMCgp100‐102 and confirmed by the Phase 3 results.

From a safety perspective, data from study IMCgp100‐202 showed that CRS mainly occurred 
within the first 3 weeks of dosing, with the majority of the CRS events being grade 2 or below 
(Table 9). From an efficacy perspective, partial responses were observed in patients receiving 
40 mcg weekly dosing and in 1 patient receiving 20 mcg IMCgp100 daily dosing, suggesting 
potential activity at 20‐ 30 mcg dose.

FDA considers that no further dose optimization on priming dose is considered necessary or 
feasible, given that CRS occurred during the first 3 weeks and with low rate of grade 3+ CRS 
(Table 9), and that the overall response rate (ORR) was low making the dose optimization effort 
challenging. In addition, a small number of patients (n=3) used tocilizumab, suggesting general

| information to understand tebentafusp’s mechanism of action. |

acceptable tolerability (with respect to CRS).

#### Table 9: Study IMCgp100‐202 Summary of weekly CRS incidence rates over time

Source: Table 2, Response to FDA IR, SDN22, Page 3. 
 
The selection of flat dosing strategy is based on result from study IMCgp100‐01. The MTD for 
weekly tebentafusp dosing was identified as 600 ng/kg. Patients dosed with 600 ng/kg 
tebentafusp received an average dose of 49.3 mcg; however, experience with study drug 
identified the potential for higher serum concentrations to occur in heavier patients with body 
weight dosing. As a result, a flat dosing was selected over body weight based dosing. 
 
The selection of weekly dosing is supported by results from study IMCgp100‐01 showing no 
clinically meaningful differences in safety or efficacy between the weekly and daily dosing 
regimens. From efficacy perspective, the profile of responses to tebentafusp treatment was 
comparable for patients treated with weekly dosing and daily dosing (9.3% vs 6.7%, Table 10). 
Partial responses were seen in 4 patients receiving 600 ng/kg and 1 patient receiving 40 mcg 
tebentafusp weekly dosing in Arm 1 and in 1 patient receiving 20 mcg tebentafusp daily dosing 
in Arm 2. In particular, all partial responses seen in patients with uveal melanoma were for 
those treated with the weekly dosing regimen. The overall response rate was 20.0% (3/15) 
(95% CI: 4.3% to 41.8%) for weekly dosing as compared to 0% (0/3) for daily dosing.

#### Table 11: Summary of Treatment‐emergent Adverse Events/Safety Population

Source: table 38, IMCgp100‐01 Clinical study report, page 128.   
 
The selection of the maintenance dose of 68 mcg dose is mainly based on results from study 
IMCgp100‐102, in which the different maintenance dose was compared by evaluating fixed low 
doses of tebentafusp at C1D1 (20 mcg) and C1D8 (30 mcg), followed by an escalated cohort‐
specified QW dose administered at C1D15 and beyond (i.e., 54, 64, 73 and 68 mcg). Two out of 
four patients at the 20/30/73 mcg experienced dose limiting toxicities (DLT) (Grade 4 AST 
increased, and ALT increased in one patient and Grade 2 and Grade 3 AST increased and Grade 
1 hyperbilirubinemia in another patient). All 3 patients recovered, and all resumed tebentafusp 
treatment at a reduced dose with no recurrence of toxicity. Given the DLTs reported at 73 mcg, 
a lower dose level of 68 mcg was tested. No DLTs were reported at this dose level, which was 
considered the MTD/RP2D for Phase 2 dose expansion.

6.3.2.2   Is an alternative dosing regimen or management strategy required for 
subpopulations based on intrinsic patient factors? 
Data:  
 
See Therapeutic Individualization Section Above 
 
The Applicant’s Position: 
No,  See Therapeutic Individualization Section Above 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s position that no dose adjustment is needed in subpopulations 
based on intrinsic patient factors or ADA status. Although the ADA formation increased the 
tebentafusp clearance and decreased tebentafusp exposure, exploratory exposure‐response 
analyses do not suggest any clinically meaningful differences in efficacy or safety between the 
ADA+ versus ADA‐ patient populations.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
|  |
| FDA agrees with the Applicant’s position that no dose adjustment is needed in subpopulations |
| based on intrinsic patient factors or ADA status. Although the ADA formation increased the |
| tebentafusp clearance and decreased tebentafusp exposure, exploratory exposure‐response |
| analyses do not suggest any clinically meaningful differences in efficacy or safety between the |
| ADA+ versus ADA‐ patient populations. |

6.3.2.3   Are there clinically relevant food‐drug or drug‐drug interactions, and what 
is the appropriate management strategy? 
Data: 
Not Applicable – iv infusion. 
 
The Applicant’s Position: 
Not Applicable – iv infusion. 
 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
Tebentafusp can cause transient release of cytokines that may potentially suppress CYP450 
enzymes. Based on evaluation of the totality of data, FDA considers the risk of drug interaction 
to be low. FDA’s conclusion is based on the following considerations:

 Tebentafusp’s half‐life of 6‐8 hours is relatively short. 
 The elevations of specific pro‐inflammatory cytokines observed after the tebentafusp

infusions are transient in nature, and attenuate with repeat dosing. 
 The highest drug‐drug interaction risk is following the first three doses of tebentafusp. 
 Label recommends that patients are required to be observed after dosing for at least 16

hours, which alleviate the risk of potential drug interaction related AEs. 
 
This conclusion is supported by the observed clinical data. In study IMCgp100‐202, twenty 
(20/392, 5.1%) tebentafusp‐treated patients with metastatic uveal melanoma were identified 
as receiving concomitant medications with narrow therapeutic index within a 2‐week period of 
a CRS episode. The rate of Grade 3 and 4 TEAEs in the selected population was comparable to 
the overall tebentafusp population and none of these patients had QTcF prolongation > 500 
msec during the susceptible period.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |  |
|---|---|
|  |  |
| Tebentafusp can cause transient release of cytokines that may potentially suppress CYP450 |  |
| enzymes. Based on evaluation of the totality of data, FDA considers the risk of drug interaction |  |
| to be low. FDA’s conclusion is based on the following considerations: |  |
|  |  Tebentafusp’s half‐life of 6‐8 hours is relatively short. |
|  |  The elevations of specific pro‐inflammatory cytokines observed after the tebentafusp |
|  | infusions are transient in nature, and attenuate with repeat dosing. |
|  |  The highest drug‐drug interaction risk is following the first three doses of tebentafusp. |
|  |  Label recommends that patients are required to be observed after dosing for at least 16 |
|  | hours, which alleviate the risk of potential drug interaction related AEs. |

### 7 Sources of Clinical Data

#### Table of Clinical Studies

Data:

The clinical development program of tebentafusp in melanoma includes 5 Immunocore-
sponsored clinical studies, 2 completed studies (Phase 1 Study 01 and Phase 2 rollover 
Study 401) and 3 ongoing studies (Phase 1/2 Study 102, Phase 1b/2 Study 201, and Phase 3 
Study 202) (Table 13). Across these clinical studies, 587 patients with melanoma, including 
410 patients with UM, have been exposed to tebentafusp monotherapy.

### 8 Statistical and Clinical Evaluation

## Review of Relevant Individual Trials Used to Support Efficacy

#### Pivotal Study 202

### Trial Design

The Applicant’s Description:

Overall design 
This is an ongoing open-label, randomized, multi-center study to evaluate the efficacy and safety 
of tebentafusp versus investigator’s choice (dacarbazine, ipilimumab, or pembrolizumab) in adult 
HLA-A*02:01-positive patients with mUM who had not received prior systemic therapy in the 
metastatic setting. Enrolled patients were randomized 2:1 to receive either tebentafusp (Arm1) or 
investigator’s choice (Arm 2), the latter of which was selected prior to randomization. 
Randomization was stratified by LDH status. The study schema is depicted in Figure 25.

Arm 1 (tebentafusp): All patients randomized to Arm 1 received tebentafusp by intravenous 
(IV) infusion following the intra-patient escalation regimen. Patients received 20 mcg on Day 1, 
30 mcg on Day 8, 68 mcg on Day 15, and 68 mcg once every week thereafter. Due to the 
anticipated cytokine release-associated toxicity with tebentafusp following the first 3 doses, 
patients were monitored for at least 16 hours after dosing as an inpatient following the weekly 
doses on Days 1, 8, and 15.

Arm 2 (investigator’s choice): All patients randomized to Arm 2 received investigator’s choice 
of one of the following 3 options: dacarbazine at the standard dosing regimen in UM of 
1000 mg/m2 given on Day 1 of each 21-day cycle; ipilimumab at the dosing regimen for 
unresectable or metastatic melanoma of 3 mg/kg given on Day 1 of each 21-day cycle for a 
maximum of 4 doses; or pembrolizumab at the dosing regimen of 2 mg/kg up to a maximum of 
200 mg or 200 mg administered IV where approved locally given on Day 1 of each 21-day cycle. 
The preferred investigator’s choice agent was selected prior to randomization. No extended 
monitoring after dosing was required in Arm 2.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

84 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

#### Figure 25

C#D# = Cycle # Day #; HLA = human leukocyte antigen; LDH = lactate dehydrogenase; Q3W = every 3 weeks; 
RP2D‐IE = recommended Phase 2 dose intra‐patient escalation regimen; ULN = upper limit of normal.  
 
Treatment continued until radiographic progression (except for patients receiving ipilimumab), 
unacceptable toxicity, investigator decision, or patient withdrawal of consent. Patients receiving 
tebentafusp, pembrolizumab, or ipilimumab experiencing disease progression per RECIST could 
continue with treatment beyond initial RECIST progression if they met the prespecified criteria. 
 
Choice of control group 
Prior to this study, no therapy has demonstrated a survival benefit in UM (Ramaiya, 2007; 
Augsberger, 2009; Khattak, 2013). In the absence of standard of care, options for UM patients 
have included PD-1 inhibitors, ipilimumab, or chemotherapy. Therefore, the comparator arm for 
this randomized study was an investigator’s choice with 3 options that included pembrolizumab, 
ipilimumab, and dacarbazine. 
 
Eligibility criteria 
Key inclusion criteria included: 
 ≥ 18 years of age at the time of informed consent. 
 Histologically or cytologically confirmed mUM. 
 No prior systemic therapy in the metastatic or advanced setting. 
 No regional liver-directed therapy. 
 HLA-A*02:01 positive by central assay. 
 ECOG performance status score of 0 or 1. 
 
Key exclusion criteria included: 
 Systemic or untreated CNS metastases. 
 History of severe hypersensitivity reactions to other iologic drugs or mAbs. 
 Clinically significant cardiac or impaired cardiac function. 
 Active infection that required systemic antibiotic therapy. 
 Known HIV.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

85 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

 Active hepatitis B virus or hepatitis C virus infection. 
 History of adrenal insufficiency. 
 History of interstitial lung disease. 
 History of pneumonitis requiring corticosteroid treatment or current pneumonitis. 
 History of colitis or inflammatory bowel disease. 
 Treatment with systemic steroid therapy or any other immunosuppressive medication at 
any dose level. 
 Radiotherapy within 2 weeks of first dose of study drug. 
 Use of hematopoietic colony-stimulating growth factors. 
 
Dose selection 
Tebentafusp 
The dosing regimen of tebentafusp used in Study 202 was 20 mcg on Day 1, 30 mcg on Day 8, 
68 mcg on Day 15, and 68 mcg once every week thereafter. Tebentafusp is administered via IV 
infusion over 15 to 20 minutes. The selection of intra-patient dose escalation over the first 
3 weeks was identified in FIH, Phase 1 Study 01 and the actual doses were selected during the 
Phase 1 portion of Study 102. The final, recommended dosing regimen was then studied in the 
Phase 2 portion of Study 102 and Study 202.

Several key observations in Study 01 led to recommending an intra-patient escalation regimen 
using fixed doses. First, in Study 01, patients with higher body weights who received higher 
absolute doses of tebentafusp experienced more severe treatment-related toxicity. Consequently, 
fixed doses, rather than weight-based doses, were incorporated during the study. Second, given 
no clinically meaningful differences in safety or efficacy were identified between the weekly and 
daily dosing regimens, and in light of the easier utility of a weekly regimen, subsequent 
evaluation focused on weekly dosing. Third, the emerging safety profile of tebentafusp suggested 
that CRS (and associated hypotension) was more likely to occur during the first 2 weeks, after 
which tachyphylaxis occurred. Therefore, as has been used for other T cell-engaging bispecifics, 
an intra-patient escalation regimen during Weeks 1 and 2 (ie, 20 and 30 mcg, respectively) prior 
to dosing 50 mcg was selected as the preferred regimen to evaluate further in the subsequent 
single-arm, Phase 1/2 Study 102.

In Study 102, the intra-patient escalation regimen based on fixed dosing identified in Study 01 
was further optimized by evaluating higher Week 3 doses (54 to 73 mcg) to achieve greater 
exposure. During the Phase 1 portion of this study, which employed a standard 3+3 dose-
escalation design, the 73 mcg dose level was not tolerated due to elevations in hepatic 
transaminases with concurrent low-grade increases in bilirubin in 2 of 4 treated patients. These 
hepatic events were reversible without administration of corticosteroids, and all patients who 
experienced dose-limiting toxicities remained on treatment. After a dose reduction to 68 mcg, 
6 patients were treated with no dose-limiting toxicities and no significant liver enzyme 
elevations. As a result, a dose of 68 mcg was identified as the maximum tolerated dose and 
selected for further evaluation as part of the intra-patient escalation regimen during the Phase 2 
portion of Study 102 and was subsequently also incorporated into Study 202.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

86 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

Investigator’s choice 
The investigator’s choice options (pembrolizumab, ipilimumab, or dacarbazine) were 
administered at approved doses and regimens for the treatment of metastatic melanoma. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s summary of the pivotal trial, Study 202. The comparator arm 
consisting of Investigator’s choice of dacarbazine, ipilimumab or pembrolizumab is considered 
appropriate and consistent with current standard of care for the systemic treatment of 
unresectable and metastatic uveal melanoma.

Analysis population).

#### Table 14: Study 202: Analysis Populations

Analysis Set 
Definition 
ITT Analysis Set 
The ITT Analysis Set comprised all patients assigned to treatment analyzed by the 
treatment assignment whether or not the patient received the assigned treatment. All 
patients randomized in the study were analyzed in the ITT population. The ITT Analysis 
Set was used for all summaries and analyses of demography, baseline characteristics, 
disposition, medical history, prior anticancer therapy, and efficacy data summaries and 
analyses. 
RAS 
The RAS comprised all patients assigned to tebentafusp who developed a rash within the 
first week of treatment (ie, Study Days 1 to 7 and prior to the second dose in case the 
second dose was received early) and all patients randomized to investigator’s choice 
regardless of rash. If the analysis for the RAS crossed the pre‐specified stopping 
boundaries and stopping boundaries for the ITT Analysis Set at the same planned analysis 
were not crossed, then this analysis set was also to be used for demography, baseline 
characteristics, efficacy, and safety data summaries and analyses. If the stopping 
boundaries for the RAS OS analysis were crossed, then summaries of demographics, 
baseline characteristics, and safety were also to be run on this analysis set. 
Safety Analysis Set 
The Safety Analysis Set included all randomized patients who received at least 1 full or 
partial dose of tebentafusp or investigator’s choice. Patients were classified in this set 
according to initial treatment received. The Safety Analysis Set was used for all safety 
summaries. 
PK Analysis Set 
The PK Analysis Set included patients in the Safety Analysis Set who had at least 1 
measurable PK concentration and who had the relevant date, time, and dosing data for 
the sample. 
ITT = Intent‐to‐treat; OS = overall survival; PK = pharmacokinetics; RAS = Rash Analysis Set. 
 
Multiple testing strategy 
To provide strong control of the type I error rate, the primary endpoint of OS and key secondary 
endpoints of PFS and BOR were to be tested in this sequential order for the ITT analyses. If any 
previous analysis in the sequence was not statistically significant, the alpha could not be transferred 
to subsequent analyses. Since neither PFS nor BOR were tested on an interim basis, both endpoints 
were tested at an overall alpha level of 0.045 (2-sided) or 0.05 if the alpha from the RAS analysis 
was transferred to the ITT analyses.

The final analysis of PFS was to be based on 274 progression and death events. Assuming a median 
PFS of 5 months in the tebentafusp arm and 3.3 months in the investigator’s choice arm, an HR of 
0.66, and the same accrual and drop-out assumptions described earlier for OS, the analysis of PFS 
was expected to have 90% power to demonstrate a difference in the survival distributions between 
the 2 arms. Due to the higher hazard of progression events relative to death events, the required 
number of PFS events was expected to occur prior to the first interim analysis of OS. If the required 
number of events did not occur at the time of the first OS interim analysis, then the PFS analysis 
was to occur at a later time when 274 progression events had occurred.

| Analysis Set | Definition |
|---|---|
| ITT Analysis Set | The ITT Analysis Set comprised all patients assigned to treatment analyzed by the treatment assignment whether or not the patient received the assigned treatment. All patients randomized in the study were analyzed in the ITT population. The ITT Analysis Set was used for all summaries and analyses of demography, baseline characteristics, disposition, medical history, prior anticancer therapy, and efficacy data summaries and analyses. |
| RAS | The RAS comprised all patients assigned to tebentafusp who developed a rash within the first week of treatment (ie, Study Days 1 to 7 and prior to the second dose in case the second dose was received early) and all patients randomized to investigator’s choice regardless of rash. If the analysis for the RAS crossed the pre‐specified stopping boundaries and stopping boundaries for the ITT Analysis Set at the same planned analysis were not crossed, then this analysis set was also to be used for demography, baseline characteristics, efficacy, and safety data summaries and analyses. If the stopping boundaries for the RAS OS analysis were crossed, then summaries of demographics, baseline characteristics, and safety were also to be run on this analysis set. |
| Safety Analysis Set | The Safety Analysis Set included all randomized patients who received at least 1 full or partial dose of tebentafusp or investigator’s choice. Patients were classified in this set according to initial treatment received. The Safety Analysis Set was used for all safety summaries. |
| PK Analysis Set | The PK Analysis Set included patients in the Safety Analysis Set who had at least 1 measurable PK concentration and who had the relevant date, time, and dosing data for the sample. |

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

88 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The analysis of BOR was to occur after all 369 randomized patients were followed for 
approximately 9 months (ie, at least 3 planned on-treatment assessments) for response. It was to 
be formally tested for statistical significance only if the null hypotheses for OS and PFS in the 
ITT Analysis Set were both rejected. 
 
Interim analyses 
Two interim analyses were to be performed using a 3-stage group sequential design. Separate 
analyses were to be performed for each of the 2 primary objectives, but the analyses were to 
occur at the same time and the timing would be driven by the number of events in the ITT 
Analysis Set. The first interim analysis was based on approximately 60% of the events 
(150 events). The second interim analysis was to be based on approximately 80% of the events 
(200 events). Analyses of OS were based on O’Brien-Fleming boundaries (O’Brien, 1979). The 
Lan-DeMets approach (Lan, 1983) that approximates the O’Brien-Fleming spending function 
was used to adjust for situations where the actual number of events up to the DCO date for a 
given interim analysis did not match the planned number.

For the first interim analysis, the RAS analysis was conducted first. If the stopping boundaries 
were crossed, then the full alpha for that analysis (α = 0.005) was added to the alpha allocated for 
the ITT analyses (α = 0.045), resulting in a total αITT = 0.05. If, at a particular interim analysis, 
stopping boundaries were crossed for the RAS analysis but not the ITT analysis, then the ITT 
alpha allocation for future analyses was adjusted, as described by Maurer and Bretz (Maurer, 
2013). Therefore, stopping boundaries for the ITT analyses were adjusted accordingly. 
Secondary endpoints such as PFS and BOR were not formally tested in the RAS and were not 
tested on an interim basis.

amendment are summarized in Table 15.

schedule

|---|---|---|
| 2 | 12 June 2020 | Further clarification of endpoints and analysis methods following the protocol amendment |

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

89 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

#### Table 15: Study 202: SAP Amendments Summary

SAP Version 
Date 
Major Changes
AESI = adverse event of special interest; CMH = Cochran‐Mantel‐Haenszel; CTCAE = Common Terminology Criteria for 
Adverse Events; DCR = disease control rate; ORR = objective response rate; PK = pharmacokinetics. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s summary of the statistical analysis plan of Study 202. In 
addition to what is included in the Applicant’s summary, additional details on sample size 
determination and analysis methods for the primary and key secondary endpoints are provided 
below.  
 
Analysis Methods: 
The difference in OS between the treatment arms was tested using a 2‐sided log‐rank test 
stratified by LDH status (LDH > ULN versus LDH ≤ ULN; measured centrally). The OS HR was 
estimated using a stratified Cox‐proportional hazards model using the Efron approach for 
handling ties, along with corresponding 95% CIs for the HR. The analysis method for PFS was 
the same as that of OS. ORR was compared between treatment arms using a stratified Cochran 
Mantel‐Haenszel (CMH) test adjusting for baseline LDH status. 
 
Sample Size: 
The sample size in Study 202 was driven by OS in the all randomized population. Assuming a 2:1 
randomization ratio of tebentafusp versus investigator’s choice, 250 events (deaths) were 
required to provide 89% power to detect an OS HR of 0.645 at 2‐sided significance level of 
0.045. Assuming OS was exponentially distributed and a median OS of 12 months in the 
investigator’s choice arm, the HR of 0.645 corresponds to a median OS of 18.6 months in the 
tebentafusp arm resulting in a difference of 6.6 months in median OS between the arms. 
Considering a non‐uniform recruitment of about 33 months and 10% annual drop‐out rate, 369 
patients were to be randomized in a 2:1 ratio to the 2 arms to observe 250 events after 51 
months as follows. This sample size accounts for two formal interim analyses of OS.

#### Protocol Amendments

The Applicant’s Description:

The original protocol was dated 12 January 2017. The global protocol was amended 4 times. 
Amendments 1 and 2 were instituted before the first patient was enrolled. The global protocol 
amendments are summarized in Table 16.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| FDA agrees with the Applicant’s summary of the statistical analysis plan of Study 202. In |
| addition to what is included in the Applicant’s summary, additional details on sample size |
| determination and analysis methods for the primary and key secondary endpoints are provided |
| below. |
|  |
| Analysis Methods: |
| The difference in OS between the treatment arms was tested using a 2‐sided log‐rank test |
| stratified by LDH status (LDH > ULN versus LDH ≤ ULN; measured centrally). The OS HR was |
| estimated using a stratified Cox‐proportional hazards model using the Efron approach for |
| handling ties, along with corresponding 95% CIs for the HR. The analysis method for PFS was |
| the same as that of OS. ORR was compared between treatment arms using a stratified Cochran |
| Mantel‐Haenszel (CMH) test adjusting for baseline LDH status. |
|  |
| Sample Size: |
| The sample size in Study 202 was driven by OS in the all randomized population. Assuming a 2:1 |
| randomization ratio of tebentafusp versus investigator’s choice, 250 events (deaths) were |
| required to provide 89% power to detect an OS HR of 0.645 at 2‐sided significance level of |
| 0.045. Assuming OS was exponentially distributed and a median OS of 12 months in the |
| investigator’s choice arm, the HR of 0.645 corresponds to a median OS of 18.6 months in the |
| tebentafusp arm resulting in a difference of 6.6 months in median OS between the arms. |
| Considering a non‐uniform recruitment of about 33 months and 10% annual drop‐out rate, 369 |
| patients were to be randomized in a 2:1 ratio to the 2 arms to observe 250 events after 51 |
| months as follows. This sample size accounts for two formal interim analyses of OS. |

formulations.

flexibility, while maintaining safe 
conduct of the study.

on the investigator’s choice arm to switch from

approved.

preventive actions were undertaken.

### Patient Disposition

Data: 
From 04 October 2017 to 18 June 2020, 447 HLA-A*02:01-positive patients were screened, of 
whom 378 patients were randomly assigned (2:1) to tebentafusp (n = 252) or investigator’s 
choice (n = 126; Figure 26) at 58 sites in 14 countries (US, Germany, France, United Kingdom, 
Poland, Canada, Australia, Belgium, Spain, Switzerland, Ukraine, Russia, Italy, and the 
Netherlands). Treatment choices available in the investigator’s choice arm were pembrolizumab 
(n = 103; 81.8%), ipilimumab (n = 16; 12.7%), and dacarbazine (n = 7; 5.6%).

As of 13 October 2020, the DCO date of the primary analysis, the median duration of follow-up 
for all patients was 14.1 months (range, 12.7 to 15.6 months).

A total of 245 patients (97.2%) in the tebentafusp arm and 111 patients (88.1%) in the 
investigator’s choice arm received at least 1 dose of study drug (Figure 26). Seven patients 
(2.8%) in the tebentafusp arm and 15 patients (11.9%) in the investigator’s choice arm were 
randomized but not treated, with the main reason being patient decision (1.6% and 11.1%, 
respectively. Of the patients who were randomized but not treated, 3 patients (42.9%) in the 
tebentafusp arm and 10 patients (66.7%) in the investigator’s choice arm continued to be 
followed for survival at the DCO. At least 6 of 10 patients (60.0%) in the investigator’s choice 
arm received anti-PD-L1/cytotoxic T lymphocyte-associated antigen-4 (CTLA-4) therapy, of 
whom 5 patients received anti-PD-L1/CTLA-4 combination therapy.

A total of 172 patients (68.3%) in the tebentafusp arm and 100 patients (79.4%) in the 
investigator’s choice arm had discontinued treatment, while 73 patients (29.0%) continued to 
receive tebentafusp and 11 patients (8.7%) continued to receive investigator’s choice (Figure 26). 
The most common reason for permanent discontinuation of study drug was PD, which occurred 
in 154 patients (61.1%) in the tebentafusp arm and 78 patients (61.9%) in the investigator’s 
choice arm.

A total of 83 patients (32.9%) in the tebentafusp arm and 41 patients (32.5%) in the 
investigator’s choice arm discontinued study treatment but remained on study (Figure 26). Study 
discontinuation was reported for 96 patients (38.1%) in the tebentafusp arm and 69 patients 
(54.8%) in the investigator’s choice arm, with the main reason for discontinuation being death 
(87 and 63 patients, respectively).

#### Protocol Violations/Deviations

Data: 
At least 1 type of important protocol deviation was reported in 99 patients (39.3%) in the 
tebentafusp arm and 36 patients (28.6%) in the investigator’s choice arm (Table 17). The most 
common (> 10% of patients) important protocol deviations in both treatment arms were related 
to trial procedures (22.6% and 11.1%, respectively).

The Applicant’s Position:

Overall, the higher rate of protocol deviations in the tebentafusp arm compared with the 
investigator’s choice arm is related to more frequent dosing (weekly vs every 3 weeks) and an 
intensive schedule of assessments and visits in the tebentafusp arm. Given the number of patients 
enrolled and the volume of data collected over the study duration, the deviations were 
determined to not impact the interpretation of the study results as they pertain to the study’s 
relevant objectives and endpoints. Moreover, the COVID-19 pandemic had no substantial impact 
on the assessment of the study objectives.

Protocol deviations were managed according to the protocol deviation guidance provided by the 
Sponsor and were reviewed by the Sponsor.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s assessment of important protocol deviations. The dataset

included 213 important violations (166 occurring on the tebentafusp arm, 45 occurring in the IC 
arm, and 2 involving use of incorrect versions of the informed consent document (ICD)

 Discontinuation criteria, including treatment past progression without signing specific

treatment past progression informed consent form, or treatment past confirmed

 Inclusion/ Exclusion criteria, including laboratory assessments not meeting criteria,

requirements. 
 Informed Consent/ HIPAA, including use of wrong ICD or failure to re‐consent with

updated ICF, screening/ screening labs prior to signing ICD,  
 Investigational Product, including patient refusal to stay overnight in hospital as

required by protocol, product administered beyond 4 hours (all < 10 minutes), missed 
doses due to freezer  or other technical problem with product, incorrect storage or 
freezer failure, administration of incorrect dose (2 events involving incorrect dosing of 
68  mg instead of 20 mg on day 1 cycle 1).  
 Prohibited medication, specifically administration of pre‐medication which was not

allowed per protocol prior to administration of C1D1 for 1 patient. 
 Delayed SAE reporting. 
 Trial procedures including missed laboratory assessments, scan completed outside of

window, missed post dose vital signs, incorrect timing of laboratory assessments. 
 
There were more Trial Procedure violations in the tebentafusp arm than occurred in the IC arm. 
This can be explained by the increased frequency of treatment, increased complexity of 
administration and monitoring, and lack of familiarity with the investigational product.  The 
violations do not necessitate removal of any patients from the analysis. The protocol deviations 
described above are unlikely to have had a meaningful impact on interpretation of the study 
results.

#### Table of Demographic Characteristics

Data: 
Overall, the majority of patients were White (87.0%) and approximately half were male (50.3%), 
with a median age of 64.0 years (range, 23 to 92 years) (Table 18). Approximately half of the 
patients were ≥ 65 years of age. Nearly two-thirds of patients were from the non-North American 
region (63.5%). By country, most patients were enrolled in the US (31.7%) and Germany 
(15.6%). The vast majority of patients (94.5%) had an ECOG performance status score of 0 or 1 
at baseline. One patient, in the investigator’s choice arm, had an ECOG performance status score 
of 2, which is an eligibility criteria deviation and was accounted for in the important protocol 
deviations.

The Applicant’s Position:

The demographic and baseline characteristics of the study population were generally well 
balanced between the 2 treatment arms. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s summary of the patients’ demographic characteristics and 
agrees that they were generally balanced across the treatment groups. The median age of 
patients in the study was 64, slightly older than what has been cited in the literature as (59 to 
62 years) (Kaliki 2017). The study included very few patients of American Indian/Alaskan Native 
race and Hispanic or Latino ethnicity. No patients were reported to be Black/African American 
or Asian, however this appears to be consistent with observed incidences of uveal melanoma in 
different racial and ethnic groups.

Other Baseline Characteristics (e.g., disease characteristics, important concomitant drugs)

Data: 
Baseline disease characteristics of the Study 202 population are summarized in Table 19. For 
most patients, the choroid was the initial UM site (75.7%) and metastasis was not observed at 
initial diagnosis (92.3%). Approximately one-third of patients had LDH > ULN 250 U/L 
(36.0%), a poor prognostic factor for advanced UM, and more than half of the patients’ largest

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

102 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The Applicant’s Position:

Baseline disease characteristics were generally well balanced between the 2 treatment arms and 
representative of a 1L mUM population. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA agrees with Applicant’s summary of patients’ disease characteristics at baseline.

#### Treatment Compliance, Concomitant Medications, and Rescue Medication Use

Data: 
Data are presented below as part of the applicant’s position. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

Treatment compliance 
The median relative dose intensity was similar in both treatment arms: 100.0% (range, 95% to 
100%) in the tebentafusp arm and 100% (range, 100% to 100%) in the investigator’s choice arm.

Concomitant medications 
Concomitant medications were defined as medications that (1) started before the first dose of 
study drug and were continuing at the time of the first dose of study drug, or (2) started on or 
after the date of the first dose of study drug (or, started at the time of or after the first dose of 
study drug) up to 90 days following the last dose.

A total of 245 patients (97.2%) in the tebentafusp arm and 108 patients (85.7%) in the 
investigator’s choice arm received at least 1 concomitant medication. The most common classes 
of concomitant medications received (by > 50% of patients in either the tebentafusp arm or 
investigator’s choice arm) were analgesics (89.7% vs 41.3%), antihistamines for systemic use 
(86.1% vs 18.3%), blood substitutes and perfusion solutions (56.7% vs 14.3%), and 
corticosteroids, dermatological preparations (54.0% vs 14.3%). The drug classes of analgesics, 
antihistamines, blood substitutes, anti-inflammatory products, and corticosteroids were received 
by a notably higher percentage of patients in the tebentafusp arm because they were used as 
preventive or therapeutic interventions for management of rash and CRS, which are AEs 
associated with the mechanism of action of tebentafusp.

Subsequent anticancer therapies 
After discontinuation of study drug, 109 patients (43.3%) in the tebentafusp arm and 55 patients 
(43.7%) in the investigator’s choice arm received other systemic anticancer therapies. The 
mediation duration of subsequent anticancer treatment was 110.0 and 70.0 days, respectively. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA agrees with the Applicant’s assessments.

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

### Efficacy Results – Primary Endpoint (Including Sensitivity Analyses)

Data: 
Overall survival – ITT Analysis Set 
In the ITT Analysis Set, based on a median follow-up duration of 14.1 months and 150 death 
events (87 [34.5%] in the tebentafusp arm and 63 [50.0%] in the investigator’s choice arm), the 
primary endpoint of OS favored tebentafusp with a HR of 0.51 (95% CI: 0.37, 0.71; p < 0.0001; 
Table 20 and Figure 27). Although not yet mature, the Kaplan-Meier estimates of median OS 
was longer in the tebentafusp arm (21.7 months; 95% CI: 18.6, 28.6) compared with the 
investigator’s choice arm (16.0 months; 95% CI: 9.7, 18.4). Kaplan-Meier estimates of OS at 
12 and 24 months were 73.2% and 44.8%, respectively, for tebentafusp, and 58.5% and 20.3%, 
respectively, for investigator’s choice (Table 20).

Overall survival sensitivity analysis 
Overall survival results were consistent across all prespecified sensitivity analyses. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

Tebentafusp demonstrated a significant improvement in OS, compared with investigator’s 
choice, in HLA-A*02:01-positive patients with mUM who had not received prior systemic 
therapy in the metastatic setting. Tebentafusp reduced the relative risk of death by 49%, 
compared with investigator’s choice (HR 0.51; 95% CI: 0.37, 0.71; p < 0.0001). Based on a 
median follow-up duration of 14.1 months, treatment with tebentafusp resulted in a 6-month 
improvement in estimates of median OS compared with investigator’s choice (21.7 vs 16.0 
months), and an approximate 15% increase in 1-year OS (73.2% vs 58.5%). Overall survival 
results were consistent across all prespecified sensitivity analyses. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
Primary analysis of OS: 
FDA generally agrees with Applicant’s summary of the primary analysis results of OS in the all‐
randomized population. FDA notes that with 150 OS events observed at this interim analysis 
(60% of the total 250 events required for final OS analysis), the corresponding stopping 
boundary was 0.006. FDA also notes that, while all the landmark/milestone rates presented for 
OS were validated by the FDA reviewers, these were considered as supportive information only.

### Efficacy Results – Secondary and other relevant endpoints

Data: 
Progression-free survival 
Based on a median follow-up duration of 11.4 months and 295 PD or death events (198 [78.6%] 
in the tebentafusp arm and 97 [77.0%] in the investigator’s choice arm), PFS favored tebentafusp 
and met statistical significance (HR 0.73; 95% CI: 0.58, 0.94; p = 0.0139) (Table 21 and Figure 
28).  Median PFS was 3.3 months in the tebentafusp arm and 2.9 months in the investigator’s

| Sensitivity analysis of OS: |
|---|
| FDA acknowledges and agrees with the Applicant’s position that OS results were consistent |
| across all prespecified sensitivity analyses. FDA notes that, as per SAP, the only planned |
| sensitivity analysis of OS included considering a stratified analysis based on strata determined |
| by the central LDH results if there are >10% discrepancies observed in LDH results when |
| compared to the strata recorded at the time of randomization in the IRT system, which was the |
| prespecified source of stratification that to be used in the primary analysis of OS. The Applicant |

| stratum and their appropriate LDH stratum per the central lab data and therefore no additional |

| analysis set. |

Best overall response, objective response rate, disease control rate 
Best overall response, ORR, and DCR are summarized in Table 22Error! Reference source not 
found..

In the tebentafusp arm, BORs were 1 CR (0.4%) and 22 PRs (8.7%); 92 patients (36.5%) had SD 
and 131 (52.0%) had PD. In the investigator’s choice arm, there were no CRs; 6 patients (4.8%) 
had PRs, 28 (22.2%) had SD, and 78 (61.9%) had PD.

The ORR was numerically higher in the tebentafusp arm (9.1%; 95% CI: 5.9, 13.4) compared 
with the investigator’s choice arm (4.8%; 95% CI: 1.8, 10.1). The prespecified time point for 
statistical comparison of BOR has not yet been reached.

Disease control rate (defined as CR + PR + SD ≥ 12 weeks) favored the tebentafusp arm 
compared with the investigator’s choice arm, with rates of 45.6% (115 of 252 patients; 95% CI: 
39.4, 52.0) and 27.0% (34 of 126 patients; 95% CI: 19.5, 35.6), respectively.

Time to response

The Applicant’s Position:

Tebentafusp demonstrated a statistically significant improvement in the secondary endpoint of 
PFS, compared with investigator’s choice. Tebentafusp reduced the relative risk of disease 
progression or death by 27%, compared with investigator’s choice (HR 0.73; 95% CI: 0.58, 0.94; 
p = 0.0139). Disease control rate at 12 weeks was numerically higher with tebentafusp than 
investigator’s choice (45.6% vs 27.0%). The point estimate for ORR was higher with tebentafusp 
than investigator’s choice (9.1% vs 4.8%). Best overall response will be formally tested in a later 
analysis after all patients have undergone at least 3 planned on-treatment tumor assessments. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment:

(b) (6)

(b) (6)

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

112 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

While FDA generally agrees with the Applicant’s summary of the secondary endpoint results, 
FDA has the following assessments regarding these results:

 FDA does not agree with the Applicant’s conclusion that tebentafusp demonstrated a

clinically significant improvement in PFS over IC in Study 202. Although the HR of 0.73 
(95% CI: 0.58, 0.94) for PFS favored the tebentafusp arm, the improvement in median 
PFS was only 0.4 months, and while the p‐value of 0.0139 would be considered 
statistically significant, FDA does not consider an improvement of less than 2 weeks to 
be clinically meaningful. The tumor responses were assessed every 12 weeks. In 
addition, the 95% CI for the PFS probability at all landmark timepoints for the 
tebentafusp and IC arms overlap. The lack of benefit with respect to PFS can also be 
noted from the KM plot of PFS curves, where separation between the curves over the 
entire follow‐up period was very marginal.  
 The tumor response rates observed in Study 202 are marginal and effectively the same

for both arms. The 95% CI’s overall with the lower bound of the 95% CI is under 6% for 
both arms.  
 
FDA also has the following additional comments :

 As per the SAP, PFS was planned to be tested only once after observing at least 275

events and therefore, the observed p‐value of 0.0139 for PFS analysis was compared to 
an alpha of 0.05 to demonstrate statistical significance.  
 FDA acknowledges that ORR was not formally tested at this interim analysis. 
 FDA does not object to the Applicant’s inclusion of DCR in their summary in this review;

however, this endpoint was not considered as part of the overall benefit:risk assessment

.  
 All the landmark/milestone rates presented for PFS and DOR were validated by the FDA

reviewers but these were considered as supportive information only.

exposure‐response. Validation of the tebentafusp regimen is provided by the Phase 3 results, 
including high OS (hazard ratio [HR] 0.51 for OS; Table 20) and overall tolerability (low rate of 
tebentafusp‐related discontinuations [2.4% Phase 2, 2.0% Phase 3] and no tebentafusp‐related

#### Persistence of Effect

Data: 
Data are presented below are part of the applicant’s position. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

The Phase 3 Study 202 is an ongoing open-label, randomized, multi-center study to evaluate the 
efficacy and safety of tebentafusp versus investigator’s choice (pembrolizumab, ipilimumab, or 
dacarbazine) in adult HLA-A*02:01-positive patients with mUM who had not received prior 
systemic therapy in the metastatic setting. All patients randomized to tebentafusp received the 
intra-patient escalation regimen of 20 mcg on Day 1, 30 mcg on Day 8, 68 mcg on Day 15, and 
68 mcg once every week thereafter. Tebentafusp was administered via intravenous infusion over 
15 to 20 minutes. Treatment continued until radiographic progression, unacceptable toxicity, 
investigator decision, or patient withdrawal of consent. Patients who received tebentafusp, 
pembrolizumab, or ipilimumab and experienced disease progression per RECIST could continue 
with treatment beyond initial RECIST progression until confirmed RECIST progression, if they 
met the prespecified criteria.

In the ITT Analysis Set, based on a median follow-up of 14.1 months, the median duration of 
treatment was 163.0 days (range, 1 to 1016 days) with tebentafusp and 65.0 days (range, 1 to 
658 days) with investigator’s choice.  A total of 172 patients (68.3%) in the tebentafusp arm and 
100 patients (79.4%) in the investigator’s choice arm had discontinued treatment, while 
73 patients (29.0%) continued to receive tebentafusp and 11 patients (8.7%) continued to receive 
investigator’s choice. The most common reason for permanent discontinuation of study drug was

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

114 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

disease progression, which occurred in 154 patients (61.1%) in the tebentafusp arm and 
78 patients (61.9%) in the investigator’s choice arm.

In Phase 3 Study 202, only patients receiving tebentafusp and, in the investigator’s choice arm, 
only patients receiving pembrolizumab were treated beyond initial RECIST progression and 
included in the treatment beyond progression analyses. No crossover to tebentafusp was 
permitted; investigators were free to choose subsequent therapy. In the ITT Analysis Set, the 
incidence of treatment beyond initial RECIST progression was higher in patients randomized to 
the tebentafusp arm compared with those randomized to the investigator’s choice arm (43.3% 
[109/252] vs 14.3% [18/126]).

To better understand the role of treatment beyond progression, a post-hoc exploratory analysis 
was conducted in the subset of patients who had a BOR of PD. Among patients with a BOR of 
PD, the incidence of treatment beyond initial RECIST progression was higher with tebentafusp 
than pembrolizumab (53.4% [70/131] vs 17.5% [11/63]). In these patients, the median duration 
of treatment beyond progression was longer with tebentafusp than pembrolizumab (1.7 vs 
0.8 months).

To eliminate immortal time bias and to capture the majority of PD patients after the first tumor 
assessment at Day 84 (± 7 days), a landmark OS analysis was conducted that was limited to 
patients with a BOR of PD alive at Day 100. Patients with a BOR of PD are traditionally 
considered to not be benefitting from therapy and by definition, do not have indolent SD, and so 
OS could not be confounded by slow growing tumor.

In this landmark OS analysis, 105 of 252 patients (41.7%) in the tebentafusp arm versus 53 of 
126 patients (42.1%) in the investigator’s choice arm were alive and had a best response of PD 
by Day 100. In these patients, OS was superior for tebentafusp compared with investigator’s 
choice (HR 0.43; 95% CI: 0.27, 0.68; Figure 31), even when considering key baseline covariates. 
These data provide a potential explanation for why tebentafusp can have a low RECIST-based 
response rate but dramatic OS benefit and suggest that radiographic-defined PD for tebentafusp 
may not always equate with lack of benefit or a reason for treatment discontinuation.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
Post hoc analyses, including those of the responder‐analysis of treatment past progression, 
were not considered as part of FDA’s overall risk:benefit assessment of tebentafusp.  
 
In general, FDA does not agree that the argument presented above supports the Applicant’s 
conclusion. A comparison of patients in the tebentafusp arm who were treated past 
progression with patients in the pembrolizumab arm who were treated past progression does 
not support a conclusion that any observed benefit was due to treatment past progression. Any 
improvement in OS observed in patients in the tebentafusp arm who were treated past 
progression when compared to patients in the pembrolizumab arm could have been derived 
before being treated past progression. To assess whether treatment past progression provides 
benefit to the patients, the Applicant must demonstrate that patients in the tebentafusp arm 
who were treated past progression had superior outcome to patients in the tebentafusp arm 
who were not treated past progression by randomly assigning the patients to these two groups.

Data: 
Health‐related quality of life 
Health-related quality-of-life data were collected using the EORTC QLQ-C30 and EQ-5D,5L 
PRO instruments.

EORTC-QLQ-C30  
In both the tebentafusp and investigator’s choice arms, patients were considered to be domain 
compliant (ie, completed at least 50% of the EORTC QLQ-C30 items) through C17D1, with 
generally similar rates between the arms. Subsequently, patients in the tebentafusp arm remained 
domain compliant through C29D1, whereas compliance in the investigator’s choice arm 
decreased to approximately 33% at C29D1.

At baseline, no differences in EORTC-QLQ-C30 scores were observed between the treatment 
arms for any of the domains. In general, throughout the study, the EORTC-QLC-C30 scores 
were similar between the treatment arms and remained stable for most domains. However, 
statistically significant and clinically meaningful LS mean improvements from baseline were 
observed for fatigue at EOT (10.9 vs 20.1; p = 0.0445) and insomnia at C5D1 (-9.3 vs 2.8; 
p = 0.0176), both favoring tebentafusp, and for constipation at EOT (3.2 vs -3.5; p = 0.0296), 
favoring investigator’s choice. LS mean scores over time are illustrated in Figure 32 for PRO 
symptoms of fatigue, insomnia, and constipation.

Figure 32

QLQ‐C30 (ITT Analysis Set)

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

118 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

EQ-5D, 5L 
In both the tebentafusp and investigator’s choice arms, patients were considered to be domain 
compliant through C17D1, with generally similar rates between the arms. Subsequently, patients 
in the tebentafusp arm remained domain compliant through C29D1, whereas compliance in the 
investigator’s choice arm decreased to 40.0% at C21D1 and 33.3% at each of C25D1 and EOT.

At baseline, no differences in EQ-5D, 5L scores were observed between the treatment arms for 
any of the domains. In general, throughout the study, mean change from baseline was similar 
between the treatment arms for all domains. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

Health-related quality of life, as assessed by the EORTC-QLQ-C30 and EQ-5D,5L PRO 
instruments, was generally similar between the 2 treatment groups, with some symptoms 
showing improvement in the tebentafusp group. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
PROs were included as secondary endpoints in Study 202; however, no PRO endpoints were 
included in the formal testing plan, so all PRO analyses are considered to be exploratory and no 
claims can be made based on these analyses. Thus, FDA does not agree with the Applicant’s 
conclusion of “statistically significant and clinically meaningful LS mean improvements from 
baseline” for specific PRO domains such as fatigue, insomnia, and constipation. FDA also does 
not agree with the Applicant’s conclusion of “no significant difference between the tebentafusp 
and investigator’s choice arms for time to sustained deterioration across the different EORTC 
QLQ‐C30 domains” and the Applicant’s statement that health related quality of life was 
generally similar between the two treatment groups. Such claims in particular cannot be made 
as the trial was not powered to show non‐inferiority and was not designed with pre‐specified 
non‐inferiority margins for the domains.  
 
FDA has the following additional comments regarding the PRO analyses for this trial:

 The EORTC‐QLQ‐C30 and EQ‐5D, 5L instruments are completed at baseline, at C1D1, at

Day 1 of every other cycle through C5D1, then every 4th cycle thereafter beginning with 
C9D1 until (and including at) end of treatment (during the treatment period).  
 FDA agrees with the Applicant’s summary of the completion rates and the domain

compliant rates as presented.  
 While EORTC‐QLQ‐C30 maybe a reasonable choice to assess some functional impacts,

the Global Health Status/QoL metric does not necessarily reflect a meaningful 
assessment of core disease, treatment symptoms, and their associated impact. 
 The EQ‐5D‐5L is a composite that incorporates self‐reported ability to function, pain,

and general health status as filled out by the patient. This instrument is a generic 
preference based measure intended to provide a health utility index value for use in 
economic analyses and lacks content validity for use in estimating clinical benefit for the

#### Additional Analyses Conducted on the Individual Trial

Data: 
Data are presented below as part of the applicant’s position. These data were also presented 
above to support persistence of effects. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

There is accumulating evidence in the field of immuno-oncology, initially described for 
ipilimumab, that some patients treated with checkpoint inhibitors may develop immune-related 
response patterns beyond traditional RECIST response. While the most widely cited example of 
this is tumor regression despite the appearance of new lesions, other examples include a slow, 
steady decline in tumor burden and initial PD of the tumor prior to subsequent disease 
stabilization (Wolchok, 2009). The practical implication is that survival benefit may still occur 
despite initial disease progression, and thus, progression should be confirmed prior to 
discontinuation of immunotherapy (Hodi, 2016).

Examples of the immune-related response patterns to tebentafusp were noted in Phase 1, with 
predominantly a slow, steady decline in tumor burden and some patients who had initial PD 
followed by disease stabilization (Middleton, 2015; Middleton, 2016). In Study 102 Phase 2 
expansion, a low RECIST response rate but promising OS coupled with examples again of these 
types of immune responses suggested that immune-related response may predominate for 
tebentafusp. Intriguingly, approximately 42% of patients (25/60) with a best RECIST response of 
PD, including some with an increase in tumor burden as best change on treatment, had survival 
longer than 1 year.

In clinical practice, standard of care for checkpoint inhibitors includes the option for treatment 
beyond initial progression because of the concept of immune-related responses. However, no 
Phase 3 study with checkpoint inhibitors has demonstrated that immune-related responses are 
sufficiently high to account for an OS benefit.

In Phase 3 Study 202, only patients receiving tebentafusp and, in the investigator’s choice arm, 
only patients receiving pembrolizumab were treated beyond initial RECIST progression and 
included in the treatment beyond progression analyses. No crossover to tebentafusp was 
permitted; investigators were free to choose subsequent therapy. In the ITT Analysis Set, the 
incidence of treatment beyond initial RECIST progression was higher in patients randomized to 
the tebentafusp arm compared with those randomized to the investigator’s choice arm (43.3% 
[109/252] vs 14.3% [18/126]).

To better understand the role of treatment beyond progression, a post-hoc exploratory analysis 
was conducted in the subset of patients who had a BOR of PD. Among patients with a BOR of

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

120 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

PD, the incidence of treatment beyond initial RECIST progression was higher with tebentafusp 
than pembrolizumab (53.4% [70/131] vs 17.5% [11/63]). In these patients, the median duration 
of treatment beyond progression was longer with tebentafusp than pembrolizumab (1.7 vs 
0.8 months).

To eliminate immortal time bias and to capture the majority of PD patients after the first tumor 
assessment at Day 84 (± 7 days), a landmark OS analysis was conducted that was limited to 
patients with a BOR of PD alive at Day 100. Patients with a BOR of PD are traditionally 
considered to not be benefitting from therapy and by definition, do not have indolent SD, and so 
OS could not be confounded by slow growing tumor.

In this landmark OS analysis, 105 of 252 patients (41.7%) in the tebentafusp arm versus 53 of 
126 patients (42.1%) in the investigator’s choice arm were alive and had a best response of PD 
by Day 100. In these patients, OS was superior for tebentafusp compared with investigator’s 
choice (HR 0.43; 95% CI: 0.27, 0.68; Figure 31), even when considering key baseline covariates. 
These data provide a potential explanation for why tebentafusp can have a low RECIST-based 
response rate but dramatic OS benefit and suggest that radiographic-defined PD for tebentafusp 
may not always equate with lack of benefit or a reason for treatment. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA does not consider post hoc analyses and does not agree with the Applicant that any 
conclusions can be made regarding efficacy in the subgroup of patients that were treated 
beyond progression. The lack of randomization is unable to account for potential differences in 
inherent patient characteristics that may influence the interpretation of this post hoc analysis. 
See FDA comment above.

#### Supportive Study 102

### Trial Design

The Applicant’s Description:

Overall design 
This was a Phase 1/2 study of tebentafusp administered on a QW basis with an intra-patient 
escalation dosing regimen (Figure 33). The intra-patient escalation regimen consisted of fixed 
low doses of tebentafusp at C1D1 (20 mcg) and C1D8 (30 mcg), followed by an escalated cohort 
specified QW dose administered at C1D15 and beyond. According to this regimen, all patients in 
the study received 2 QW doses of tebentafusp at a dose level below the identified RP2D-QW 
(50 mcg; determined in Study IMCgp100-01), and then dose escalation commenced at the third 
QW dose at C1D15 with the goal to achieve a long-term dosing regimen at a dose higher than 
that identified for the straight QW dosing regimen (RP2D-QW). Doses between 54 and 73 mcg 
were evaluated in the Phase 1 dose escalation cohorts. Dose escalation identified the RP2D-IE; 
68 mcg was selected for Phase 2 dose expansion.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| FDA does not consider post hoc analyses and does not agree with the Applicant that any |
| conclusions can be made regarding efficacy in the subgroup of patients that were treated |
| beyond progression. The lack of randomization is unable to account for potential differences in |
| inherent patient characteristics that may influence the interpretation of this post hoc analysis. |
| See FDA comment above. |

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

121 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

#### Figure 33

IV = intravenous(ly). 
 
The Phase 1 portion of the study had a standard 3 + 3 dose escalation design. After the dose 
escalation portion was complete and the MTD or the RP2D-IE was identified, two Phase 2 dose 
expansion cohorts in mUM were to be enrolled. The Phase 2 dose expansion Cohort A was to 
enroll patients with mUM in the second-line setting after disease progression following systemic 
treatment with a checkpoint inhibitor and to recruit approximately 20 patients. Phase 2 dose 
expansion Cohort B was to enroll patients with mUM in the second- or third-line settings with up 
to 1 prior line of LDT and to recruit approximately 130 patients. However, in practice, there was 
significant overlap between the Cohort A and Cohort B populations, and it was not clear that 
patients belonged distinctly in either cohort. Therefore, this report will present data for the single 
combined Phase 2 dose expansion cohort. This expansion cohort was designed to further 
characterize the safety, tolerability, and preliminary PK and antitumor activity of tebentafusp. 
 
Eligibility criteria 
Key inclusion criteria included: 
 ≥ 18 years of age at the time of informed consent. 
 Histologically or cytologically confirmed mUM. 
 Cohort A: Disease progression on 1 systemic treatment regimen containing a checkpoint 
inhibitor. Any prior LDT was acceptable.1 
 Cohort B: Disease progression on 1 or 2 prior lines of therapy, including chemotherapy, 
immunotherapy, or targeted therapy. Prior LDT was counted as a line of therapy.1 
 HLA-A*02:01 positive by central assay. 
 ECOG performance status score of 0 or 1. 
 
Key exclusion criteria included: 
 Systemic or untreated CNS metastases.

1 In practice, there was significant overlap between Cohort A and Cohort B populations, and it was not clear that patients 
belonged distinctly in either cohort. Therefore, the data were presented for a single combined Phase 2 expansion cohort.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

122 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

 History of severe hypersensitivity reactions to other iologic drugs or mAbs. 
 Clinically significant cardiac or impaired cardiac function. 
 Active infection that required systemic antibiotic therapy. 
 Known HIV. 
 Active hepatitis B virus or hepatitis C virus infection. 
 Adrenal insufficiency. 
 Treatment with systemic steroid therapy or any other immunosuppressive medication at 
any dose level. 
 Radiotherapy within 2 weeks of first dose of study drug. 
 Use of hematopoietic colony-stimulating growth factors. 
 Systemic anticancer therapy within 2 weeks of the first dose of study drug. 
 Requiring chronic, systemic corticosteroid therapy at any dose for longer than 2 weeks. 
 
Dose selection 
The selection of intra-patient dose escalation over the first 3 weeks was identified in FIH, 
Phase 1 Study 01. Several key observations in Study 01 led to recommending an intra-patient 
escalation regimen using fixed doses. First, in Study 01, patients with higher body weights who 
received higher absolute doses of tebentafusp experienced more severe treatment-related 
toxicity. Consequently, fixed doses, rather than weight-based doses, were incorporated during 
the study. Second, given no clinically meaningful differences in safety or efficacy were 
identified between the weekly and daily dosing regimens, and in light of the easier utility of a 
weekly regimen, subsequent evaluation focused on weekly dosing. Third, the emerging safety 
profile of tebentafusp suggested that CRS (and associated hypotension) was more likely to occur 
during the first 2 weeks, after which tachyphylaxis occurred. Therefore, as has been used for 
other T cell-engaging bispecifics, an intra-patient escalation regimen during Weeks 1 and 2 (ie, 
20 and 30 mcg, respectively) prior to dosing 50 mcg was selected as the preferred regimen to 
evaluate further in Study 102.

#### Statistical Analysis Plan and Amendments

The Applicant’s Description:

Analysis populations 
Four analysis sets were used in this study, as defined inTable 24.

#### Table 24: Study 102: Analysis Populations

Analysis Set 
Definition 
All Patients Enrolled 
Set 
The All Patients Enrolled Set comprised all patients who provided the main informed 
consent for this study. Patients who signed prescreening informed consent but not the 
main informed consent did not appear in this analysis set. The All Patients Enrolled Set 
was used to summarize patient disposition and the analysis sets. Any patients who 
signed the main informed consent, but never started the study drug for any reason were 
regarded as screen failures. For these patients, the eCRF data collected was not to be 
included in summary analyses but was to be reported in the clinical study report as part 
of the listings for patient disposition, treatment allocation and eligibility criteria. 
Full Analysis Set 
The FAS comprised all patients assigned to study drug and who received at least 1 full or 
partial dose of tebentafusp. The FAS was used for all demography, baseline 
characteristics, and efficacy data summaries and analyses. 
Safety Analysis Set 
The Safety Analysis Set included all patients who received at least 1 full or partial dose of
tebentafusp. Patients were classified in this set according to initial treatment received. 
The Safety Analysis Set was used for the safety summary of the study. 
Per‐protocol Set 
The PPS consisted of a subset of FAS patients in the Phase 2 dose expansion cohort who 
met the following criteria: 
 Presence of measurable disease at baseline according to Investigator assessment 
based on RECIST v1.1. 
 One or more postbaseline tumor assessment or discontinue prior to the first tumor 
assessment. 
 Received at least 1 full or partial dose of treatment. 
 No violation of key inclusion or exclusion criteria as described in the SAP. 
Patients in the PPS were classified according to planned treatment. The PPS defined the 
patients used in the sensitivity analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint (ie, ORR) and 1 
of the secondary endpoints (DOR) for the Phase 2 dose expansion cohort only. 
DOR = duration of response; FAS = Full Analysis Set; ORR = objective response rate; PPS = Per‐protocol Set; 
RECIST = Response Evaluation Criteria in Solid Tumors; SAP = statistical analysis plan. 
 
SAP amendments

amendment are summarized in Table 25.

| Analysis Set | Definition |
|---|---|
| All Patients Enrolled Set | The All Patients EnrolledSet comprised all patients who provided the main informed consent for this study. Patients who signed prescreening informed consent but not the main informed consent did not appear in this analysis set. The All Patients Enrolled Set was used to summarize patient disposition and the analysis sets. Any patients who signed the main informed consent, but never started the study drug for any reason were regarded as screen failures. For these patients, the eCRF data collected was not to be included in summary analyses but was to be reported in the clinical study report as part of the listings for patient disposition, treatment allocation and eligibility criteria. |
| Full Analysis Set | The FAS comprised all patients assigned to study drug and who received at least 1 full or partial dose of tebentafusp. The FAS was used for all demography, baseline characteristics, and efficacy data summaries and analyses. |
| Safety Analysis Set | The Safety Analysis Set included all patients who received at least 1 full or partial dose of tebentafusp. Patients were classified in this set according to initial treatment received. The Safety Analysis Set was used for the safety summary of the study. |
| Per‐protocol Set | The PPS consisted of a subset of FAS patients in the Phase 2 dose expansion cohort who met the following criteria:  Presence of measurable disease at baseline according to Investigator assessment based on RECIST v1.1.  One or more postbaseline tumor assessment or discontinue prior to the first tumor assessment.  Received at least 1 full or partial dose of treatment.  No violation of key inclusion or exclusion criteria as described in the SAP. Patients in the PPS were classified according to planned treatment. The PPS defined the patients used in the sensitivity analysis of the primary efficacy endpoint (ie, ORR) and 1 of the secondary endpoints (DOR) for the Phase 2 dose expansion cohort only. |

Implemented new DLT criterion for transient 
Grade 3 ALT and/or AST elevations to be

exclude any patient with a history of adrenal

corticosteroid treatment.

corticosteroid therapy for any reason 
were excluded due to the potential 
dysfunction of the hypothalamic‐
pituitary‐adrenal axis in mediating 
response to stress. 
Amendment 4 
dated 
07 Sep 2016

Given encouraging emerging clinical safety and 
efficacy data with tebentafusp in UM where a 
strong signal of disease stabilization has been 
observed in early dosing cohorts in this study, 
the sample size of the RP2D‐IE expansion cohort 
was increased from 20 to 40 patients. Also, 
changed the inclusion criteria for the RP2D‐IE 
expansion cohort to include approximately 40 
patients treated in the second‐line setting 
following disease progression with a checkpoint 
inhibitor.

To provide a larger safety dataset and 
more robust point estimate of overall 
survival in the selected patient 
population.

allele expression. 
To require central testing for the HLA‐
A*02:01 allele expression. 
Implemented new translational work in the 
Phase 2 RP2D‐IE cohort. 
To assess the predictive and 
pharmacodynamic impact of changes 
in circulating tumor DNA with UM 
mutations in GNAQ and GNA11.

dated 
11 Apr 2017

Updated the protocol‐specified doses of 
tebentafusp throughout the protocol. This 
included updates to the 60, 70, 75, and 80 mcg 
dose. 
Updated AE management guidance was 
provided, including updated management of the 
events of cytokine release syndrome and 
hypotension.

To reflect the conduct of the dose 
escalation cohorts and updated 
protocol‐specified dose levels.

Amendment 6 
dated 
15 Dec 2017

Increased the sample size of the Phase 2 dose 
expansion cohorts (from approximately 
40 patients to approximately 150 patients) and 
added the primary endpoint of the single‐arm 
Phase 2 dose expansion cohort of ORR assessed 
by independent central review based on RECIST 
v1.1. Two separate expansion cohorts were 
defined based on prior therapy. Given the formal 
efficacy measures implemented in this dose 
expansion cohort, the study was designated as a 
Phase 1/2 to reflect this new endpoint.

Based on the observation of durable 
partial responses and minor responses 
(defined as a tumor response where 
the SLD of target lesions is reduced by 
10% to 29%) in the dose escalation 
cohorts of this study, and to provide a 
formal analysis of the antitumor 
efficacy in this patient population.

Clarified the criteria for treatment beyond 
progression and treatment discontinuation in the 
circumstance of treatment beyond progression 
using modified irRECIST. The rationale for 
treatment beyond progression was provided.

To provide additional detail delineating 
criteria for treatment beyond 
progression.

Clarified that an IDMC would review the safety 
data from the Phase 2 dose expansion cohorts 
on an ongoing basis and would also review both 
efficacy and safety after approximately 
75 patients have been recruited to cohort.

To monitor the benefit‐risk profile of 
tebentafusp.

Added patient reported outcomes to screening 
assessments (EQ‐5D,5L and EORTC QLQ‐C30 
questionnaires). 
Added additional guidance for the management 
of treatment‐related toxicity including 
hypotension and cytokine release events (that 
were generally observed 2 to 24 hours after the 
dose of tebentafusp), rash, and pruritus. 
Clarified that antitumor response as assessed by 
irRECIST was an exploratory endpoint.

Clarification

The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA acknowledges and agrees with the Applicant’s summary of key elements and the trial 
design for Study 102.  
 
The Applicant met with FDA on October 12, 2018, to discuss the proposed development plan 
and registrational strategy for tebentafusp. During this meeting, the Applicant proposed an 
accelerated approval pathway supported by ORR data (with a target lower 95% confidence limit 
of ≥ 5% for confirmed ORR) submitted from Study 102 and supportive data from Study 202 
available at the time of the planned interim analysis of Study 102.  
 
FDA expressed uncertainty whether an ORR endpoint from a single‐arm trial would be able to 
accurately and reliably predict clinical benefit in the intended patient population and whether 
the proposed target effect, that would exclude a lower 95% confidence limit of ≥ 5% for
