For more comprehensive discussion of cardiac toxicity see Section 8.2.5.  
 
Based on review of shifts for PR, QRS, and RR interval abnormalities provided in the CSR for 
Study 202, FDA agrees with the Applicant. There were no clinically meaningful trends in ECG 
findings.

#### QT

The Applicant’s Position:

In Study 102 and Study 202, there were no clinically meaningful trends in ECG findings and 
associated cardiac AEs.   
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
Based on review of the analysis of ECGs provided in the CSR for Study 202, FDA does not find 
any evidence that tebentafusp is associated with meaningful or persistent QT prolongation.  As 
stated in the CSR, a total of 4 patients (1.6%) in the tebentafusp arm and no patients in the IC 
arm had post baseline QTcF values > 500 msec.  Of the 4 patients in the tebentafusp arm, 3 of 
them had baseline values ≤ 450 msec and 1  patient had a baseline between 450 and 480 msec.  
All 4 cases of prolonged QTcF were observed pre‐dose (i.e., 1 week from the last dose of 
tebentafusp) were transient, and returned to < 450 msec at the next time point (i.e., 1 hour 
post‐dose).  In addition, 7 patients of patients in the tebentafusp arm (2.9%) and no patients 
who received IC had an increase from baseline in QTcF > 60 msec. The Applicant states that 
none of these QTcF changes were associated with clinically significant or reported cardiac 
disorders. Narratives for patients with post baseline QTcF values > 500 msec were reviewed.

#### Immunogenicity

The Applicant’s Position:

Overall, there was no meaningful impact of ADA on either patient safety or efficacy, based on 
frequency or grade of hypersensitivity AEs before and after ADA onset.  Treatment-emergent 
ADA were detected in 4% of patients in study IMCgp100-01 using a first-generation assay and 
limited sampling strategy. In later studies where a more robust assay and sampling strategy were 
employed, treatment-emergent ADA were detected in 33% and 29% of mUM patients in studies 
IMCgp100-102 and IMCgp100-202, respectively. In these studies, ADA had a median onset 
time of 6 (study IMCgp100-102) and 9 weeks (study IMCgp100-202) after the first dose of 
tebentafusp, and median titers of 8192 (study IMCgp100-102) and 2050 (study IMCgp100-202).

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| For more comprehensive discussion of cardiac toxicity see Section 8.2.5. |
|  |
| Based on review of shifts for PR, QRS, and RR interval abnormalities provided in the CSR for |
| Study 202, FDA agrees with the Applicant. There were no clinically meaningful trends in ECG |
| findings. |

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| Based on review of the analysis of ECGs provided in the CSR for Study 202, FDA does not find |
| any evidence that tebentafusp is associated with meaningful or persistent QT prolongation. As |
| stated in the CSR, a total of 4 patients (1.6%) in the tebentafusp arm and no patients in the IC |
| arm had post baseline QTcF values > 500 msec. Of the 4 patients in the tebentafusp arm, 3 of |
| them had baseline values ≤ 450 msec and 1 patient had a baseline between 450 and 480 msec. |
| All 4 cases of prolonged QTcF were observed pre‐dose (i.e., 1 week from the last dose of |
| tebentafusp) were transient, and returned to < 450 msec at the next time point (i.e., 1 hour |
| post‐dose). In addition, 7 patients of patients in the tebentafusp arm (2.9%) and no patients |
| who received IC had an increase from baseline in QTcF > 60 msec. The Applicant states that |
| none of these QTcF changes were associated with clinically significant or reported cardiac |
| disorders. Narratives for patients with post baseline QTcF values > 500 msec were reviewed. |

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

207 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The majority of these ADA responses were de novo treatment-induced responses that persisted 
after onset. A small number of patients developed high titer ADA (≥ 8192) that resulted in 
increased tebentafusp clearance and reduced Cmax exposure. However, there was no clinically 
relevant impact of ADA on either patient safety or efficacy, based on frequency or grade of 
hypersensitivity AEs before and after ADA onset, or changes in OS or tumor shrinkage by ADA 
status or titer, respectively. Thus, monitoring of ADA is not necessary.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
See Appendix 19.5. Key conclusions of FDA analysis are:  
1. Immunogenicity positive subgroup did not show significant reduced efficacy compared with

immunogenicity negative subgroup. However, the result should be considered with caution 
due to the limited number of patients (N=30) in ADA 8 weeks positive subgroup. 
2. The high titer immunogenicity positive subgroup did not show significant reduced efficacy

compared with the immunogenicity negative or low titer subgroup. However, the result 
should be considered with caution due to the limited number of patients (N=11) in high titer 
subgroup.

#### Analysis of Submission‐Specific Safety Issues

#### 8.2.5.1

Data: 
To ensure consistency, this section summarizes programmatically derived CRS using the ASTCT 
2019 consensus criteria rather than investigator-reported CRS.  
 
In Study 202, which forms the largest dataset of programmatically derived CRS events, 89% of 
patients experienced any grade CRS. Most patients had Grade 1 (12%) or Grade 2 (76%) CRS. 
One patient (0.4%) in the tebentafusp treatment arm had an event of CRS that resulted in 
discontinuation of study drug. The incidence of Grade 3 CRS was 0.8% (2 patients). There was 
no Grade 4 CRS or death due to CRS. Common symptoms of CRS included pyrexia (64.9%), 
hypotension (24.9%) and infrequently hypoxia (0.4%). Other commonly associated symptoms 
included chills (29%), nausea (19.6%), vomiting (13.5%), fatigue (12.2%), and headache 
(10.6%). 
 
Table 58 summarizes AESI of CRS programmatically identified as per ASTCT 2019 CRS 
consensus grading for tebentafusp in UM patients for Studies 102 and 202 and both studies 
combined. In Study 202, the maximum Grade 1 - 4 CRS were: 29 (11.84%), 186 (75.92%), 2 
(0.82%), and 0 (0%), (respectively).

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

209 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

Treatment‐emergent adverse events are defined as any adverse event with a start date from day of first dose of 
study drug up to 90 days after last dose of study drug or until start of alternative cancer therapy post treatment 
discontinuation, whichever occurs first. 
CRS is based on the adjudication of potential CRS episodes in Studies 102 and 202 only using the ASTCT consensus 
CRS grading criteria. 
All other AESIs are graded according to CTCAE (version 4.03). 
Source: Module 5.3.5.3, Table ISS 02.03.08.04.01. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

CRS is an important identified risk based on the mechanism of action of tebentafusp. CRS was 
graded based on the ASTCT consensus grading for CRS (Lee, 2019).  
 
Most cases of CRS occurred approximately within 1 day of tebentafusp infusion and mostly after 
the first initial doses of tebentafusp. There were too few patients with Grade ≥ 3 CRS to reliably 
interpret a median time to onset or resolution. The incidence and severity decreased with 
repeated dosing. In the vast majority of cases, CRS started the day of infusion. Pyrexia was noted 
in nearly all cases of CRS, and in these patients, an increase in body temperature generally 
occurred within the first 8 to 10 hours after tebentafusp infusion. CRS rarely (1.2%) led to 
treatment discontinuation. Most cases of CRS of any grade or Grade ≥ 2 severity, resolved by the 
day after most recent tebentafusp infusion. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
Cytokine release syndrome (CRS) is an expected class safety issue for biological products that 
engage T‐cells. Drug‐induced CRS is a clinical diagnosis based on fever ≥ 38oC with or without 
hypotension and/or hypoxia with a temporal relationship to a treatment with a drug 
mechanistically known to provoke production of proinflammatory cytokines (Shimabukuro‐
Vorhagen, 2018). CRS can start within minutes or hours of the first dose and up to 14 days after 
infusion, depending on the specific drug product.

Constitutional symptoms (headache, fatigue, arthralgias, myalgias, nausea or rash) are common 
but not required for diagnosis of CRS. Severe cases may include respiratory failure, hypotension 
requiring vasopressors, cardiac dysfunction, renal failure, elevated transaminases, and 
disseminated intravascular coagulation. CRS may result in fatal multiple system organ 
dysfunction.

Laboratory findings can include cytopenias, elevated creatinine and liver enzymes, abnormal 
coagulation parameters, and elevated CRP and ferritin.  Laboratory abnormalities can be highly 
variable and nonspecific and may lag after clinical changes.  A diagnosis of CRS does not rely on 
laboratory findings.

There are multiple grading systems for CRS in use. Initially, in Study 102 and Study 202, 
reporting of CRS was based on NCI CTCAE 4.03 criteria, shown in Table 60. In October 2017, the 
Lee CRS grading criteria (Lee, 2014), shown in Table 61, was incorporated into both studies.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| Cytokine release syndrome (CRS) is an expected class safety issue for biological products that |
| engage T‐cells. Drug‐induced CRS is a clinical diagnosis based on fever ≥ 38oC with or without |
| hypotension and/or hypoxia with a temporal relationship to a treatment with a drug |
| mechanistically known to provoke production of proinflammatory cytokines (Shimabukuro‐ |
| Vorhagen, 2018). CRS can start within minutes or hours of the first dose and up to 14 days after |
| infusion, depending on the specific drug product. |
| Constitutional symptoms (headache, fatigue, arthralgias, myalgias, nausea or rash) are common |
| but not required for diagnosis of CRS. Severe cases may include respiratory failure, hypotension |
| requiring vasopressors, cardiac dysfunction, renal failure, elevated transaminases, and |
| disseminated intravascular coagulation. CRS may result in fatal multiple system organ |
| dysfunction. |
| Laboratory findings can include cytopenias, elevated creatinine and liver enzymes, abnormal |
| coagulation parameters, and elevated CRP and ferritin. Laboratory abnormalities can be highly |
| variable and nonspecific and may lag after clinical changes. A diagnosis of CRS does not rely on |
| laboratory findings. |
| There are multiple grading systems for CRS in use. Initially, in Study 102 and Study 202, |
| reporting of CRS was based on NCI CTCAE 4.03 criteria, shown in Table 60. In October 2017, the |
| Lee CRS grading criteria (Lee, 2014), shown in Table 61, was incorporated into both studies. |

#### Table 60: CTCAE 4.03 Cytokine Release Syndrome Grading Criteria

Grade 
Symptoms 
1 
Mild reaction; infusion interruption not indicated intervention not indicated

2

Therapy or infusion interruption indicated but responds promptly to symptomatic 
treatment (e.g., antihistamines, NSAIDS, narcotics, IV fluids); prophylactic medications 
indicated for ≤ 24 hours.

3

Prolonged (e.g., not rapidly responsive to symptomatic medication and/or brief 
interruption of infusion); recurrence of symptoms following initial improvement; 
hospitalization indicated for clinical sequelae (e.g., renal impairment, pulmonary 
infiltrates) 
4 
Life‐threatening consequences; pressor or ventilatory support indicated 
5 
Death

#### Table 61: Lee Cytokine Release Syndrome Grading Criteria1

#### Grade

1 
Symptoms are not life‐threatening and require symptomatic treatment only (e.g., 
fever, nausea, fatigue, headache, myalgia, and malaise)

2

Symptoms require and response to moderate intervention: 
 
Oxygen requirement < 40% 
 
Hypotension responsive to fluids or 1 low‐dose vasopressor 
 
Grade 2 organ toxicity

3

Symptoms require and response to aggressive intervention: 
 
Oxygen requirement > 40% 
 
Hypotension requiring high‐dose or multiple vasopressors 
 
Grade 3 organ toxicity 
 
Grade 4 transaminitis

4

Life‐threatening symptoms 
 
Requirement for ventilator support 
 
Grade 4 organ toxicity (excluding transaminitis) 
5 
Death

event of CRS, with 20 patients (8%) having a maximum Grade 1 event, 29 patients (12%) having

infusion‐related reactions. One patient had an event of CRS that resulted in discontinuation of 
study drug.

To support a more complete analysis of CRS associated with tebentafusp, the Applicant 
performed a retrospective analysis based on ASTCT 2019 CRS grading criteria, shown in Table 
62. For the analysis, the Application utilized investigator TEAE reporting, vital signs, 
concomitant medications, and laboratory assessments to identify potential cases of CRS.  To 
identify potential cases of CRS, the Applicant considered the following for each patient infusion:

 Investigator report of a SAE of any of the following preferred terms on the day of the

infusion and up to 2 days afterwards: cytokine release syndrome, cytokine storm, 
infusion related reaction, pulmonary edema, adverse drug reaction, hypersensitivity 
reaction, drug hypersensitivity, systemic inflammatory response syndrome, acute 
distress syndrome event.

 Fever: considered positive if patient had an investigator report of “pyrexia” or

“tachycardia” on the day of the infusion or up to 2 days afterwards OR patient received 
an antipyretic as recorded in the concomitant medications on the day of the infusion 
and up to 3 days afterwards OR patient had record of maximum temperature ≥ 380 C as 
recorded in the vital signs on the day of or within 2 days of the infusion.

 Hypotension: considered positive if the patient had an investigator report of

“hypotension” or “diastolic hypotension” OR systolic blood pressure < 90 mm/Hg as 
recorded in the vital signs on the day of or within 2 days of the infusion.

 Hypoxia: considered positive if the patient had an investigator report of “hypoxia”,

“acute respiratory syndrome”, or “dyspnea” on the day of or within 2 days of the 
infusion OR the patient received oxygen as reported in the concomitant medications on 
the day of or within 3 days of the infusion.

 Vasopressor use: considered positive if the patient received norepinephrine,

epinephrine, dopamine, dobutamine, vasopressin, or phenylephrine as reported in the 
concomitant medications on the day of or within 3 days of the infusion.

 Steroid use:  considered positive if the patient received a corticosteroid for systemic use

as reported in the concomitant medications on the day of or within 3 days of the 
infusion.

 IV Fluid use: considered positive if the patient received fluids via IV as reported in the

concomitant medications on the day of or within 3 days of the infusion.

| infusion‐related reactions. One patient had an event of CRS that resulted in discontinuation of |

Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the

A spreadsheet of these events was then evaluated by a panel of oncologists experienced with 
CRS which graded each potential case based on the information provided. Additional 
information for pre and post vital signs was available. Out of the initial 1127 records of 
potential cases of CRS in the tebentafusp arm, the panel assessed 805 events occurring in 217 
patients as being ≥ Grade 1. The remaining records did not meet ASCTC criteria for CRS. Thus, 
89% of patients (217/245)  in the tebentafusp arm had at least 1 episode of CRS based on an 
algorithmic adjudication process using ASCTC consensus criteria. The cases comprised 29 
patients (12%) with maximum Grade 1 CRS, 186 patients (76%) with maximum Grade 2 CRS, 
and 2 patients (0.8%) with maximum Grade 3 CRS. There were no Grade ≥ 4 events.

#### Table 62: ASCTC 2019 Cytokine Release Syndrome Consensus Grading Criteria1

Symptoms 
1 
 
Temperature ≥ 380 C (not attributable to other cause) with 
 
No hypotension, hypoxia 
2 
 
Temperature ≥ 380 C (not attributable to other cause) with 
 
Hypotension not requiring vasopressors and/or 
 
hypoxia requiring low‐flow nasal canula or blow‐by 
3 
 
Temperature ≥ 380 C (not attributable to other cause) with 
 
Hypotension requiring a vasopressor with or without vasopressin and/or 
 
hypoxia requiring high‐flow nasal canula, facemask, nonrebreather mask, or 
venturi mask 
4

 
Temperature ≥ 380 C (not attributable to other cause) with 
 
Hypotension requiring multiple vasopressors (excluding vasopressin) and/or 
 
hypoxia requiring positive pressure (e.g., CPAP, BiPAP, intubation and 
mechanical ventilation. 
1 Lee et. al., 2019a

An analysis of CRS events by infusion number (week number) shows that the percentage of 
patients experiencing Grade ≥ 2 CRS (out of the total number of patients receiving tebentafusp 
that week) is highest during the first 3 infusions with the frequency dropping off drastically 
after infusion 3 (Cycle 1 Day 15). This is shown in Figure 41 below.

A patient could have more than one CRS event. Considering only Grade ≥ 2 events, the median 
number of CRS events for an individual patient was 2 with a range of 1 to 12 events.]

| A spreadsheet of these events was then evaluated by a panel of oncologists experienced with |
|---|
| CRS which graded each potential case based on the information provided. Additional |
| information for pre and post vital signs was available. Out of the initial 1127 records of |
| potential cases of CRS in the tebentafusp arm, the panel assessed 805 events occurring in 217 |
| patients as being ≥ Grade 1. The remaining records did not meet ASCTC criteria for CRS. Thus, |
| 89% of patients (217/245) in the tebentafusp arm had at least 1 episode of CRS based on an |
| algorithmic adjudication process using ASCTC consensus criteria. The cases comprised 29 |
| patients (12%) with maximum Grade 1 CRS, 186 patients (76%) with maximum Grade 2 CRS, |
| and 2 patients (0.8%) with maximum Grade 3 CRS. There were no Grade ≥ 4 events. |

The primary interventions used for CRS are oxygen, IV fluids, steroids, and vasopressor(s). The 
percentage of patients requiring these interventions for CRS related to at least 1 infusion is 
shown in Table 63. The most commonly administered intervention was IV fluids with 40% of 
patients receiving IV fluids for at least one infusion. Twenty‐four percent (24%) of patients on 
the tebentafusp arm received steroids for CRS related to at least 1 infusion. Use of oxygen and 
vasopressor(s) were rare.

Table 64 summarizes narratives for the 4 patients who received tebentafusp on Study 202 who 
had a Grade 3 event of CRS either by investigator reporting (2 patients) or Applicant‐

Table 64: Narratives for Grade 3 Cytokine Release Syndrome Study 202 Tebentafusp Arm

#### Patient ID

Source: Investigator 
Reporting (Lee’s Criteria)

66 year old woman who received 1 dose of tebentafusp.  Following 
the dose, the patient experienced an SAE of Grade 3 CRS. Signs and 
symptoms included pyrexia, hypotension, and dyspnea.  The patient 
was treated with IV fluids, hydrocortisone, oxygen (< 6 L/min), and 
acetaminophen.  No use of vasopressors was reported. The patient 
also experienced transient Grade 3 transaminase increase, Grade 3 
atelectasis, and Grade 3 metabolic acidosis. The event of CRS 
resolved 5 days after onset. 
 
 
Source: Investigator 
Reporting (Lee’s Criteria)

The patient experienced an SAE of Grade 3 CRS after the first dose of 
tebentafusp. Signs and symptoms included pyrexia, hypotension, 
shaking, and vomiting. The patient was treated with 
methylprednisolone and IV fluids. No use of vasopressors was 
reported. The event of CRS resolved 2 days after onset.  The patient 
received a total of 16 doses of tebentafusp and discontinued due to 
disease progression. 
 
 
Source: Applicant‐
adjudicated (ASCTC criteria)

68 year old gentleman who experienced Grade 3 CRS following C2D1 
dosing of tebentafusp. Signs and symptoms included pyrexia and 
hypotension. The patient was treated with IV fluids, acetaminophen, 
and oxygen (94%‐98% fraction of inspired oxygen. The event of CRS 
resolved the next day. The patient received a total of 20 doses of 
tebentafusp and discontinued due to disease progression.  
 
 
Source: Applicant‐
adjudicated (ASCTC criteria)

58 year old woman who experienced Grade 3 CRS following the first 
dose of tebentafusp. Signs and symptoms included pyrexia, 
hypotension, and dyspnea. The patient was treated with IV fluids and 
dopamine. Hypotension resolved the following day. The patient 
received a total of 14 doses of tebentafusp and discontinued due to 
progressive disease. 
Source: Reviewer summaries based on Narratives submitted with Study 202 CSR and Clinical Summary 
of Safety

Reviewer Comment: The actual frequency of CRS in patients receiving tebentafusp is not 
known. The investigator reporting of 21% of patients with at least one CRS event likely 
underestimates the frequency, while the ASCTC based Applicant adjudicated calculation of 89% 
of patients having at least one CRS event likely overestimates the frequency. The true 
frequency may be closer to the 77% calculation which considers only Grade ≥ 2 ASCTC Applicant

215 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

adjudicated CRS. Analysis of only Grade ≥ 2 events is reasonable as patients with Grade 1 CRS 
do not require intervention beyond possible administration of antipyretic.

While CRS is common in patients receiving tebentafusp, Grade 3 events were rare, and across 
Studies 202 and 102, there was only 1 case of Grade 4 CRS in which a patient developed multi‐
organ system failure. While the CRS resolved, the multi‐organ system failure persisted and was 
ongoing at the time the patient died from progressive disease.

While use of IV fluids on Study 202 was common and may have reflected protocol guidelines 
which specified IV fluids for Grade 1 hypotension and allowed administration of IV fluids prior 
to tebentafusp administration, use of oxygen and vasopressor(s) were rare.

Because CRS has the potential to be a serious and fatal condition, CRS has been included in 
Section 5 (Warnings and Precautions) and in a Black Box warning in the USPI to inform 
prescribers of the association between tebentafusp and CRS. The labeling provides information 
with respect to monitoring and treatment of CRS. Immunocore has also voluntarily developed a 
communication plan to inform clinicians who will prescribe tebentafusp regarding the risk of 
CRS.

a Determined by the investigator to be possibly related, probably related, definitely related, or related to

TEAEs are defined as any AE with a start date from day of first dose of study drug up to 90 days after last dose of 
study drug or until start of alternative cancer therapy post treatment discontinuation, whichever occurs first.

Patients with multiple events in the same category are counted only once in that category. Patients with events 
in more than 1 category are counted once in each of those categories.

a Determined by the investigator to be possibly related, probably related, definitely related, or related to 
tebentafusp.  
Patients with multiple TEAEs of special interest per category or PT are counted only once in each row. 
AEs are coded using MedDRA version 23.1.  
TEAEs are defined as any AE with a start date from day of first dose of study drug up to 90 days after last dose of 
study drug or until start of alternative cancer therapy post treatment discontinuation, whichever occurs first. 
Number (%) of patients are sorted by sponsor‐provided order for category and by descending frequency overall 
for PT. A patient can have one or more PTs reported under a given category. 
Acute skin toxicities are specified by a sponsor‐provided list of preferred terms.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

219 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The Applicant’s Position:

Acute skin reactions have been reported with tebentafusp infusion, likely based on its mechanism 
of action and gp100 expression in normal melanocytes in the skin.

For all studies combined, 379 patients (92.4%) experienced an event of acute skin reaction. Of 
the 379 patients, 377 patients (92.0%) reported an acute skin reaction that was considered related 
to study drug. CTCAE Grade 3 acute skin reaction events considered related to study drug were 
reported in 86 patients (21.0%). Serious TEAEs of acute skin reactions considered drug related 
were reported in 18 patients (4.4%). No patients experienced a TEAE of acute skin reaction that 
led to discontinuation or death. TEAEs (PTs) of acute skin reaction with the highest incidence (≥ 
10% of patients in tebentafusp arm) were pruritus (71.2%), rash (50.2%), rash maculo-papular 
(32.0%), erythema (25.6%), skin exfoliation (21.0%), and periorbital oedema (19.5%).

Acute skin reactions typically occurred following each of the first three infusions, with 
decreasing severity and frequency. The median time to onset of acute skin reactions was 1 day in 
the tebentafusp treated patients and median time to improvement to ≤ Grade 1 was 6 days. There 
were no discontinuations of tebentafusp due to acute skin reactions. Majority of symptoms 
resolved without any systemic corticosteroid or any long term sequalae. No cases of Stevens-
Johnson syndrome or toxic epidermal necrolysis were reported.

Acute skin reactions were managed with antihistamine and topical corticosteroids. Systemic 
steroids were used for persistent or severe symptoms.

The FDA’s Assessment:

Acute skin reactions associated with tebentafusp include the subcategories of rash, pruritis, 
pigment change, erythema, edema, dry skin, and other changes.

The list of PTs for the composite term rash used by the Applicant Study 202 included blister, 
dermatitis, dermatitis acneiform, dermatitis allergic, dermatitis bullous, dermatitis contact, 
dermatitis exfoliative, dermatosis, drug eruption, eczema, eczema eyelids, erythema 
multiforme, excoriation, exfoliative rash, interstitial granulomatous dermatitis, lichenification, 
lichenoid keratosis, palmar‐plantar erythrodysaesthesia syndrome, papule, prurigo, psoriasis, 
rash, rash erythematous, rash generalised, rash macular, rash maculo‐papular, rash papular, 
rash pruritic, rash vesicular, seborrhoea, seborrheic dermatitis, skin abrasion, skin erosion, skin 
exfoliation, skin irritation, skin plaque, solar dermatitis, toxic skin eruption, and urticaria.

FDA agrees with the composition of the Applicant’s group term rash. FDA validated the 
frequency for the AESI skin toxicity and the individual component PTs for Study 202 without 
regard to investigator assigned causality. Table 67 summarizes the frequency of rash 
(composite term) by grade for Study 202.  There were no Grade ≥ 4 events. In the tebentafusp 
arm, 12 patients (4.9%) had AESI of rash that were considered SAEs, 4 patients (1.6%) had AESI

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

221 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

#### 8.2.5.3

The Applicant’s Position:

LFT elevations are not uncommon in mUM since the liver is the predominant site of 
hematogenous spread from uveal melanoma. Tumor progression within the liver can result in 
liver injury with a rise in LFTs (Diener-West 2004, Eskelin 1999).

Hepatocytes do not express gp100 and tebentafusp did not redirect T cells against normal 
hepatocytes in nonclinical in vitro studies. However, treatment with tebentafusp may result in 
transient secondary effects from tebentafusp-induced inflammation in mUM liver lesions, 
including either activated immune cells (e.g., T cells) or cytokines.

Due to the number of patients enrolled, optimal schedule of laboratory collection and 
comparative AE and laboratory data, Study 202 provides the best reference for characterization 
of changes of laboratory values over time and reporting of adverse events.

In Study 202, based on investigator reported target and non-target lesions, greater than 95% of 
patients had baseline liver metastases and nearly two thirds of tebentafusp treated patients 
(158/245; 64.5%) and approximately half of investigator choice treated patients (53/111; 47.7%) 
had an increase in post-baseline grade of ALT/AST. Although numerically higher, the majority 
of ALT/AST elevations in the tebentafusp treatment arm were mild, occurred early, and did not 
result in treatment discontinuation. Since most patients had pre-existing liver metastases, LFT 
elevations may be secondary to T cell redirection into liver metastases.

No deaths due to ALT/AST elevations were observed and more than 90% of patients were able 
to continue treatment beyond worst grade ALT/AST elevation. Most patients experiencing Grade 
3 or 4 ALT/AST elevations had improvement to ≤ Grade 1 within 7 days. Elevations in bilirubin 
have been reported in 27% of patients and these were primarily associated with increase in size 
of liver metastasis.

Across all studies, patients with largest liver lesion ≥ 3 cm or values > upper limit of normal 
(ULN) for LDH and alkaline phosphatase (ALP) at baseline were at higher risk of developing 
elevated LFTs during treatment. However, this may have been due to the poor prognostic nature 
of these baseline variables and that these patients are more likely to have disease progression of 
their liver lesions as a likely cause of the on-treatment LFT increase.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
The Applicant identified cases of hepatotoxicity using the Standardized MedDRA Query (SMQ, 
Broad and narrow) Drug related hepatic disorders. Table 68 summarizes drug related hepatic 
disorders by grade for Study 202.  In the tebentafusp arm, 11 patients (4.4%) had hepatotoxicity 
AESIs, as identified by SMQ, that were SAEs. In the tebentafusp arm, hepatotoxicity AESIs, as 
identified by SMQ, resulted in withholding of study drug in 13 (5%) of patients and permanent 
discontinuation of study treatment in 1 patient (0.4%).

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| The Applicant identified cases of hepatotoxicity using the Standardized MedDRA Query (SMQ, |

| identified by SMQ, resulted in withholding of study drug in 13 (5%) of patients and permanent |

Reviewer Comment: Abnormalities in liver tests were common in patients receiving 
tebentafusp. This may have been due to CRS or underlying liver metastases. Overall, however, 
the abnormalities were mild and did not require discontinuation of study treatment. However, 
due to the frequency of events and the potential for serious outcomes Elevated Liver Enzymes 
were included in Section 5 (Warnings and Precautions) of the USPI.

#### 8.2.5.4

Data:

Patients with UM have baseline recurrent or persistent local ocular events relating to their 
primary treatment (e.g., enucleation, complication of RT, intravitreal anti-VEGF therapy). In 
addition, eye disorders were initially identified as a risk since gp100 positive intra-ocular 
melanocytes could serve as a target for tebentafusp which in theory may lead to uveitis or vision 
changes. As a result, detailed baseline and on-study ophthalmologic exams were incorporated 
into Study 01.

No concerning or related intra-ocular clinical findings or overt vision changes were identified per 
detailed ophthalmologic exams. Most reported eye AEs were extra-ocular and due to 
inflammation or peri-orbital skin AEs, including periorbital oedema (41 patients, 48.8%), eye 
pain (3 patients, 3.6%), and eye pruritus (3 patients, 3.6%). All reported ophthalmologic AEs 
were of CTCAE Grade 1 or 2. The periorbital AEs are consistent with tebentafusp redirecting T 
cells to gp100-positive melanocytes in the skin, do not impact vision, are reversible and have 
been observed in tebentafusp treated patients in all studies.

In Study 202, a total of 79 patients (32.2%) in the tebentafusp arm and 15 patients (13.5%) in the 
investigator’s choice arm had events in the SOC of eye disorders. Events with the highest 
incidence (≥ 3% of patients in either the tebentafusp or investigator’s choice arms) were 
periorbital edema (10.6% vs 0.9%) and lacrimation increased (3.3% vs 1.8%). Grade ≥ 3 events 
were reported in 3 patients (1.2%) in the tebentafusp arm and 2 patients (1.8%) in the 
investigator’s choice arm and included cataract, eye pain, glaucoma (0.4% vs 0% each), retinal

#### 8.2.5.5

Data:

In Study 102 in the Phase 1 dose escalation cohorts, cardiac disorders (regardless of causality) 
were reported in 4 (21.1%) patients. Cardiac AEs related to ECG abnormalities included 
tachycardia in 2 (10.5%) patients and sinus tachycardia in 1 (5.6%) patient; these events were 
Grade 1 or 2 in severity, non-serious, and did not result in discontinuation of study drug.

In Study 102 in the Phase 2 dose expansion cohort, cardiac disorders (regardless of causality) 
were reported in 38 (29.9%) patients. The most commonly reported (> 1% of patients) cardiac 
AEs related to ECG abnormalities were tachycardia (11.8%), sinus tachycardia in (9.4%), sinus 
bradycardia (3.9%), atrial fibrillation (3.1%), and atrial flutter (2.4%), and supraventricular 
tachycardia (1.6%). No AEs of torsades de pointes were reported. Cardiac AEs of Grade ≥ 3 
severity were reported in 7 patients (5.5%); events related to ECG abnormalities (each in 1 
patient, 0.8%) included Grade 3 and Grade 4 atrial fibrillation, atrial flutter, and tachycardia; all 
were considered treatment-related. Two patients experienced cardiac AEs that led to treatment 
discontinuation: one patient with grade 4 atrial fibrillation after day 1 of study treatment [Patient 
] and a second patient with grade 3 left ventricular dysfunction after day 8 of study 
treatment [Patient 
]. Both of these cardiac AEs occurred in the setting of sponsor 
assessed Grade 3 CRS and were considered related to tebentafusp treatment by the investigator. 
No events of Grade 5 severity were reported. Five patients experienced SAEs related to ECG 
abnormalities.

In Study 202, a total of 37 patients (15.1%) in the tebentafusp arm and 8 patients (7.2%) in the

investigator’s choice arm had events in the SOC of cardiac disorders. The event with the highest 
incidence (≥ 3% of patients in either the tebentafusp or investigator’s choice arms) was 
tachycardia (9.8% vs 2.7%). Events were considered treatment-related by the investigator in 27 
patients (11.0%) in the tebentafusp arm and 3 patients (2.7%) in the investigator’s choice arm. 
All treatment-related events were Grade 1 or 2 in severity and included tachycardia (9.0% vs 
0%), sinus tachycardia (2.4% vs 0.9%), atrioventricular block, bradycardia (0.4% vs 0% each), 
and palpitations (0% vs 1.8%). There were no clinically meaningful trends in ECG findings and 
associated cardiac AEs in either treatment arm. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

During the pre-BLA administrative meeting, the US FDA requested that along with QT 
assessment, narratives for patients with arrythmias, syncope, or with QTcF values > 500 msec 
should be provided with the BLA submission.

Given tebentafusp induces mild to moderate CRS, not surprisingly, the most frequent cardiac 
AEs were pyrexia, hypotension and tachycardia. Due to the anticipated risk of hypotension, 
Studies 102 and 202 required patients with pre-existing hypertension to temporarily suspend 
anti-hypertensive medications prior to the first few doses. Therefore, hypertension resulting from 
interruption of daily anti-hypertensives was occasionally observed during the first few weeks of 
treatment and reported as an AE. This hypertension is considered an iatrogenic AE and distinct 
from the mechanism of action of tebentafusp.

Serious cardiac disorders were reported in 0 patients in the tebentafusp arm and 1 patient (0.9%) 
in the investigator’s choice arm. The patient in the investigator’s choice arm who received 
dacarbazine (Patient 
) had a serious event of left ventricular dysfunction that resulted in 
study drug discontinuation and death; the event was considered as not related to study drug. 
Besides the event of left ventricular dysfunction on the investigator choice arm, none of the other 
events in the cardiac disorders SOC resulted in study drug discontinuation.

In Study 102 and Study 202, there were no clinically meaningful trends in ECG findings and 
associated cardiac AEs.

The FDA’s Assessment:

FDA agrees with the Applicant’s assessment of cardiac toxicity.

#### 8.2.5.6 Neurotoxicty

The FDA’s Assessment

Neurotoxicity, including potentially life‐threatening or fatal events, is an identified complication 
associated with T‐cell engager therapies, including anti‐CD19 CAR‐T cells, bi‐specific T cell 
engagers (Zheng et. al., 2019). Although neurotoxicity was not considered an AESI for Study 202

### Safety Analyses by Demographic Subgroups

The Applicant’s Position:

Across all studies, there were no clinically meaningful differences in the safety profile of 
tebentafusp vs investigator’s choice with respect to age, sex, race, and ECOG performance 
status. No overall differences in safety were observed between patients ≥ 65 years of age 
compared to younger adult patients. The onset of the first AESI was not notably different among 
the subgroups. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
TEAEs by Sex 
 
Table 69 summarizes AEs for the tebentafusp arm of Study 202 by sex. There are no significant 
differences between males and female with regards to occurrence of TEAEs. Analysis comparing 
the frequency of individual TEAEs by age in the tebentafusp arm identified the following 
differences:

 The following TEAEs were observed more frequently in females than males (≥ 15%

difference): rash (64% versus 46%), alopecia (18% versus 0), vomiting (38% versus 22%).

 No TEAEs were observed more frequently in males than females (≥ 15% difference): 
 
Some differences are to be expected due to chance alone and given the limited number of 
patients in each group, a true interaction between sex and these differences cannot be 
concluded. Thus, no sex specific labeling is indicated.

#### Specific Safety Studies/Clinical Trials

Data: 
Study 401 was a Phase 2, open-label, multi-center rollover study conducted to provide continued 
access to tebentafusp treatment for patients enrolled in a completed clinical study (Study 01) of 
tebentafusp. A total of 3 patients, all from the Study 01 parent study, were enrolled in this 
rollover study. All 3 patients were white, 2 were male and 1 was female, and their age ranged 
from 49 to 71 years. All patients had advanced melanoma with stage IV disease. Patients 
received 2, 18, and 26 cycles of tebentafusp with treatment durations of 43, 505, and 728 days. In

Following long-term exposure, the safety profile of tebentafusp was tolerable, manageable, and 
consistent with observations from other tebentafusp studies.

patients to provide meaningful additional safety information.

#### Human Reproduction and Pregnancy

#### Data:

The Applicant’s Position:

Due to the specificity for human targets, embryo-fetal development (EFD) studies cannot be 
conducted in nonclinical species. Therefore, a weight of evidence assessment was conducted to 
evaluate the risk of tebentafusp administration on pregnancy and embryo-fetal development. A 
literature search revealed that gp100 is expressed embryonically in melanocytes found in the 
skin, inner ear, and eyes by 7 weeks of gestation, and MHC Class I classical proteins (including 
HLA-A*02:01) and transporter-associated-with-antigen-processing (TAP) proteins required for 
presentation of antigen on the cell surface are expressed very early in embryonic development.  
In addition, CD3-positive T cells begin to populate the periphery and are capable of being 
activated by around 12 weeks of gestation.

However, tebentafusp’s ability to directly affect embryo-fetal development requires that 
tebentafusp crosses the placenta and gains access to the fetus.  The molecular weight of 
tebentafusp is 77 kDa, therefore, it is much too large to cross the placenta by diffusion. It also 
does not contain an Fc domain and, therefore, cannot bind to the neonatal Fc receptor (FcRn), 
which facilitates transfer of IgG molecules across the placenta, nor does it have domains that

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|
| Study 401 was not evaluated as part of FDA’s assessment of safety as there were too few |
| patients to provide meaningful additional safety information. |

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

230 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

could bind to other placental transporters. Thus, tebentafusp would not be able to gain access to 
or elicit pharmacologic activity directly in the embryo/fetus. There is also no evidence that 
tebentafusp could interfere with implantation or the maintenance of pregnancy through its 
mechanism of action.

Based on the results of this weight of evidence assessment, tebentafusp would not be expected to 
adversely affect embryo-fetal development or the maintenance of pregnancy when administered 
during pregnancy.   
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA does not agree.  There is data that biologics with a similar mechanism of action and 
molecular weight cross the placenta. See Section  5.1 of this review. The labeling was therefore 
amended to include in Warnings and Precautions (new Section 5.4 of KIMMTRAK Prescribing 
Information) information that there is a risk that tebentafusp may cause harm when 
administered to a pregnant woman.  See Section 11.

Pediatrics and Assessment of Effects on Growth
 
Data: 
Not applicable. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

Overdose, Drug Abuse Potential, Withdrawal, and Rebound 
 
Data: 
There has been no experience of overdosage with tebentafusp or evidence of drug abuse with 
tebentafusp from clinical studies. 
 
The Applicant’s Position:

There is no specific treatment for tebentafusp overdose and symptoms of overdose have not been 
established. Tebentafusp is unlikely to be abused due to its mode of action, physiological and 
pharmacological activity, lack of stimulant properties, and clinical setting of use. Because 
tebentafusp has no known potential for dependence, withdrawal or rebound events are not

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

232 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The Applicant’s Position:

Overall, tebentafusp has a well-established safety profile across the 5 Immunocore-sponsored 
clinical studies in 587 patients with melanoma, including 410 patients with UM, who were 
exposed to tebentafusp monotherapy. The randomized Study 202 provides the primary safety 
data and is proposed to be the basis for labeling presentation of Warning and Precautions and 
Adverse Events sections of the USPI. While the Study 102 safety data are consistent with Study 
202 and supportive of the proposed indication and dosing regimen.

The safety profile of tebentafusp in mUM in Study 202 and Study 102 Phase 2 expansion was 
consistent with that observed in the pooled UM and CM populations, and no new safety signals 
were identified. The rate of permanent study drug discontinuation due to tebentafusp-related AEs 
was low in both studies (2.0% and 2.4%, respectively), and there were no treatment-related 
deaths among the 372 patients treated with tebentafusp in these two studies.

Overall, the most frequent TEAEs were associated with the mechanism of action of tebentafusp. 
These included skin AEs (e.g., rash, pruritus, and erythema), presumably resulting from T cells 
redirected to gp100+ melanocytes in the skin, and cytokine-mediated AEs, due to T cell 
activation. The most clinically relevant cytokine mediated AE is CRS, which is summarized 
using the most recent, and widely used, ASTCT 2019 consensus grading criteria. The proposed 
management algorithm for acute skin reactions and for CRS were based on those used in Study 
102 and Study 202.

Most CRS events were mild to moderate with a low frequency of severe events, despite no 
requirement for primary prophylaxis with corticosteroid, antihistamine, or acetaminophen. The 
monitoring and management algorithm for rash and CRS used in the Phase 2 and 3 programs 
were successful based on low rate of drug related discontinuation, no drug related deaths and 
striking overall survival (OS) benefit. The majority of these AEs had onset within 1 day after the 
first 3 doses of tebentafusp when the patient was undergoing extended monitoring for at least 16 
hours. As has been observed for other T cell engaging bispecifics, the CRS underwent 
tachyphylaxis with repeated dosing.

In first line mUM patients in Study 202, tebentafusp significantly improved OS compared to 
investigator’s choice in the ITT analysis. The strong association between rash in Week 1 and OS 
benefit from tebentafusp suggests that rash may be a marker that the immune system can be 
mobilized by tebentafusp to target gp100+ cells. However, rash should not be used for clinical 
management since most patients develop a rash, rash was not independent of baseline prognostic 
features, and patients without a rash may still have better OS than similar patients in the control 
arm.

The other notable TEAE was LFT elevations, which were observed in both arms of Study 202 
although with higher incidence in the tebentafusp arm (i.e., nearly two-thirds of patients). Liver 
function test elevation is a common feature of mUM since > 95% of patients had pre-existing 
liver metastases. The higher incidence of LFTs following tebentafusp, which occurred in a 
similar time frame to both cytokine increase and T cell trafficking to the liver tumors, may be 
due to spill over cellular inflammation from the UM lesions in the liver and injury to adjacent

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

233 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

hepatocytes or due to elevated cytokines. Elevations in LFTs typically occurred after the first 
few doses of tebentafusp and generally were transient and manageable with treatment 
interruption alone. No safety signal was observed in cardiac or eye disorders that would require 
specific labeling.

In a subset analysis, a trend for a higher risk of elevated LFTs was observed where patients with 
largest liver lesion >3 cm, elevated LDH, or elevated ALP at baseline. However, this may have 
that these patients are more likely to have disease progression of their liver lesions as a likely 
cause of the on-treatment LFT increase. In addition, these baseline factors are also known poor 
prognostic features in mUM.

mUM is a life-threatening disease with a dismal prognosis. There are currently no effective 
treatments for mUM that extend survival, and no standard of care exists. Tebentafusp is a first-
in-class bispecific gp100-targeted TCR fusion protein that can redirect polyclonal T cells to 
target gp100+ tumor cells leading to T cell activation and release of inflammatory mediators. 
Tebentafusp monotherapy provides a dramatic OS benefit in HLAA*02:01-positive patients with 
mUM. The safety profile of tebentafusp administered at the proposed dosing regimen is 
acceptable, with a very low rate of treatment-related discontinuations and no treatment-related 
deaths. AEs are consistent with mechanism of action of tebentafusp, predictable, generally 
reversible, and clinically manageable with appropriate surveillance and intervention. The totality 
of the data supports a positive benefit-risk profile of tebentafusp as a novel treatment option for 
HLAA*02:01-positive adult patients with unresectable or mUM.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
The evaluation of the safety of tebentafusp at the proposed dosage in patients with metastatic 
uveal melanoma was based primarily on 356 patients randomized in Study 202 who received at 
least one dose of study drug (tebentafusp: 245 patients; IC: 111 patients). The Applicant 
included in their portion of the safety review analysis of data from 2 supportive trials (Study 01, 
Study 102 Phase 1 cohorts, Study 102 Phase 2 cohorts) and a pooled analysis (N= 410) 
comprised of all patients from these studies and the 245 patients who received at least one 
dose of tebentafusp on Study 202 . FDA’s assessment of safety included an analysis using a 
pooled set of 505 patients with cutaneous or uveal melanoma who received at least 1 dose of 
tebentafusp monotherapy on a clinical study (Study 01: 84 patients; Study 102: N= 146; Study 
201: N=30; Study 202: N=245). 
 
Study 202 excluded patients < 18 years of age, with a serum creatinine > 1.5 X ULN and/or 
creatinine clearance (calculating using Cockcroft‐Gault formula, or measured) < 50 mL/minute, 
clinically significant cardiac disease or impaired cardiac function, history of HIV infection, active 
HBV or HCV infection, or history of adrenal insufficiency, interstitial lung disease, pneumonitis 
that required corticosteroid treatment or current pneumonitis, history of colitis of 
inflammatory bowel disease. 
 
In Study 202, the median exposure was 163 days (range 1 day to 1016 days) in the tebentafusp

arm compared to 65 days (range 1 day to 658 days) in the IC arm. Table 71 summarizes the 
overall safety profile of tebentafusp at the proposed dosage as observed on Study 202.  
 
Overall, tebentafusp was well tolerated with a very low rate of fatal TEAEs in Study 202 and 
across the development program, with no deaths identified as likely related to study drug 
based on review of available narratives and available data. The percentage of patients receiving 
tebentafusp on Study 202 who had at least one SAE was high but comparable to that observed 
with the IC.  Over 50% of patients receiving tebentafusp on Study 202 had at least one Grade 3‐
4 TEAE. This was higher than observed in the IC arm. While SAEs and Grade 3‐5 TEAEs were 
common in patients in the tebentafusp arm in Study 202, they rarely lead to permanent 
discontinuation, which was infrequent at 3.3%.  A significant percentage of patients receiving 
tebentafusp had at least TEAE that lead to treatment interruption; however, this was 
comparable to that observed on the IC arm.

TEAE analysis of the ISS_Pool yielded similar results to what was seen in the tebentafusp arm 
for Study 202 with the exception of SAEs which was 8% higher in the ISS_Pool.  The lower rate 
in Study 202 may represent improved management guidelines for CRS provided in Study 202.

Adverse reactions associated with tebentafusp are primarily those associated with CRS 
including pyrexia, chills, nausea, vomiting, abdominal pain, hypotension, and those associated 
with skin reactions considered related to tebentafusp’s mechanism of action. These skin 
reactions include rash, dry skin, and pruritis. Worsening laboratory abnormalities, including 
both hematologic, metabolic, and chemistry assessments were common and associated with 
CRS. They were usually transient. Only for lymphocyte count decreased was the percentage of 
patients with Grade 4 laboratory abnormality ≥ 5%.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

235 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The most important adverse reaction associated with tebentafusp is CRS. While there were no 
fatalities identified across the development program considered related to CRS, there were 2 
cases of Grade 4 CRS associated events (0.8%) in the ISS_Pool, both being cases of multiple 
system organ dysfunction. In Study 202, the most commonly administered management 
interventions for CRS were IV fluids and steroids. Vasopressor(s) were rarely required. 
 
Other than the rare and life‐threatening CSR related event of multiple system organ 
dysfunction noted above, analysis of the ISS_Pool dataset did not identify any new or more 
serious safety already identified in Study 202. 
 
The safety profile of tebentafusp at the proposed dosage in patient with advanced or 
metastatic uveal melanoma who have not received prior systemic therapy in the metastatic 
setting is acceptable with most adverse reactions being Grade 1 or 2  and higher grade toxicities 
adequately managed through temporary medical intervention or treatment interruption. 
 
SUMMARY AND CONCLUSIONS

#### Statistical Issues

The FDA’s Assessment: 
No major statistical issues were identified while reviewing the data and results submitted in this 
application. Note that despite the statistically significant results observed for PFS, FDA 
considers the difference in PFS observed between the treatment arms was not clinically 
meaningful. ORR analysis was not formally tested at this interim look.

Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

## Conclusions and Recommendations

The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA concludes that the results of Study 202 demonstrate that tebentafusp provides a 
statistically significant and clinically meaningful improvement in overall survival in patients who 
were randomized to receive tebentafusp compared to patients randomized to receive 
Investigator’s Choice therapy.  Overall survival is considered by FDA to be an acceptable 
endpoint to demonstrate the effectiveness of new therapeutics across oncology indications.  
Study 202 provides the evidence that supports the effectiveness of tebentafusp in patients with 
metastatic uveal melanoma who have not received prior systemic therapy in the metastatic 
setting. The safety profile of tebentafusp at the proposed recommended dosage of 20 mcg on 
Day 1, 30 mcg on Day 8, 68 mcg on Day 15, and 68 mcg once every week thereafter is 
acceptable in the context of patients with a serious and life‐threatening condition and limited 
treatment options and is manageable with guidelines provided in product labeling. Overall, the 
review team deems the benefit: risk assessment of tebentafusp in the indicated population to 
be favorable and recommends regular approval for the following indication:

KIMMTRACK is a bispecific peptide‐HLA‐directed CD3 T cell engager indicated for the treatment 
of HLA‐A*02:01‐positive adult patients with unresectable or metastatic uveal melanoma.

### 10 Pediatrics

The Applicant’s Position:

Tebentafusp has received FDA agreement for the initial pediatric study plan for tebentafusp on 
23 March 2021. The Sponsor has submitted a request for full pediatric waiver for tebentafusp to 
the BLA based on nonrelevance of gp100 as a molecular target for any pediatric cancers.

The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA concurs.

### 12   Risk Evaluation and Mitigation Strategies (REMS)

The FDA’s Assessment: 
The risks of tebentafusp are acceptable in the indicated patient population with a serious and 
life‐threatening condition; the safe use of tebentafusp can be adequately implemented in the 
post‐marketing setting through product labeling that includes a black box warning for the risk 
of CRS. FDA requested the Applicant provide a plan to further communicate the risk of CRS to 
health care providers beyond product labeling though the distribution of a Dear Health Care 
Provider Letter. The Applicant agreed with this request and has provided the letter and a plan 
to distribute the letter to all health care providers expected to prescribe and manage treatment 
of tebentafusp outside the clinical trial setting.

| The FDA’s Assessment: |
|---|

| life‐threatening condition; the safe use of tebentafusp can be adequately implemented in the |
| post‐marketing setting through product labeling that includes a black box warning for the risk |
| of CRS. FDA requested the Applicant provide a plan to further communicate the risk of CRS to |

### 13   Postmarketing Requirements and Commitment

The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
The review team recommends issuing the following postmarketing requirement (PRMs) and 
postmarketing commitments (PMCs) 
 
Clinical Pharmacology PMC:

## 1.  Conduct an assessment to determine the presence of neutralizing anti‐drug antibodies

against tebentafusp‐tebn in all patient samples that tested positive for binding anti‐drug 
antibodies in studies IMCgp100‐202 and IMCgp100‐102 by using the validated 
neutralizing anti‐drug antibody assay. Include an assessment of the clinical impact of the 
neutralizing anti‐drug antibodies on pharmacokinetics, efficacy and safety of 
tebentafusp‐tebn in the study report. 
 
Clinical PMC:

## 1. Conduct an assay validation study to demonstrate that the assay can accurately

differentiate HLA‐A*02:01 from other HLA A alleles for identification of patients with 
uveal melanoma who may benefit from treatment with Kimmtrak (tebentafusp‐tebn) 
and use the data to support an FDA approved companion diagnostic HLA typing assay 
patient selection test.

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

250 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

### 17   Division Director (Clinical)

I agree with the clinical, statistical, non‐clinical, pharmacology, and CMC recommendations with 
respect to the approvability of BLA 761228 as well as for the demonstrated favorable risk‐
benefit assessment for tebentafusp‐tebn. 
 
Tebentafusp‐tebn (referred to as tebentafusp) is a bispecific biological product designed to bind 
to gp100 peptide presented by human leukocyte antigen‐A*02:01 (HLA‐A*02:01) on the cell 
surface of uveal melanoma tumor cells. Tebentafusp exerts its anti‐tumor effect by redirecting 
T cells to attack the gp100‐expressing tumor cells. The applicant for this BLA (Immunocore) 
seeks marketing authorization for tebentafusp for the treatment of HLA‐A*02:01‐positive adult 
patients with unresectable or metastatic uveal melanoma. The proposed dosing regimen is 20 
mcg on Day 1, 30 mcg on Day 8, 68 mcg on Day 15, and 68 mcg once every week thereafter, via 
intravenous infusion over 15‐20 minutes. 
 
The epidemiology of uveal melanoma is described above in this review. Briefly, Immunocore 
submitted data from one randomized clinical trial, Study 202, to support the approval of 
tebentafusp. Study 202 demonstrated a clinically meaningful and statistically significant 
improvement in overall survival (OS) in patients who received tebentafusp compared to those 
who received investigator’s choice of therapy which included dacarbazine, pembrolizumab, or 
ipilimumab [HR of 0.51 (95% CI: 0.37, 0.71), p < 0.0001; with a median OS of 21.7 (18.6, 28.6) 
months in the tebentafusp arm versus 16.0 (9.7, 18.4) months in the control arm]. The results 
were robust (e.g., p value less than 0.01) and clinically significant and therefore consistent with 
FDA’s requirement to demonstrate substantial evidence of effectiveness. Furthermore, I believe 
it would not be feasible or ethical to require a second randomized clinical trial, in this very rare 
malignancy without effective available therapies, prior to approval.  
 
The adverse event profile of tebentafusp is extensively described above in this review. CRS, 
dermatological, and hepatic toxicities are important adverse reactions related to tebentafusp. 
Although important and potentially life threatening, the effect observed on overall survival 
supports a favorable risk‐benefit assessment for the overall population of HLA‐A*02:01‐positive 
adult patients with unresectable or metastatic uveal melanoma.  
 
Tebentafusp will be prescribed by oncologists who are trained in the monitoring and 
management of drugs known to cause life threatening toxicities (including CRS). Risk 
minimization strategies include a Black Box Warning for CRS, specific instructions in labeling for 
monitoring and management, and a Medication Guide. In addition, health care providers that 
will be responsible for prescribing or managing patients receiving tebentafusp will receive a 
“Dear Health Care Provider” letter to increase awareness of the risk of CRS. The OMEPRM 
review provides an extensive discussion of REMS considerations; differences between

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

251 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

tebentafusp and blinatumomab (which has a REMS); and that a REMS was not considered 
necessary to ensure the benefits of tebentafusp outweigh its risks.  
 
Finally, although tebentafusp will be indicated for HLA‐A*02:01‐positive adult patients, at the 
time of approval, there will not be an FDA approved/cleared in vitro companion diagnostic 
device to select patients for treatment. Although not available, HLA typing has been conducted 
for years in clinical practice (with accurate results necessary for allogeneic stem cell transplants 
and certain solid organ transplants). Nevertheless, Immunocore has committed, via a PMC, to 
conduct an assay validation study to demonstrate that the assay can accurately differentiate 
HLA‐A*02:01 from other HLA A alleles. This PMC is intended to support the availability of an in 
vitro companion diagnostic device. Importantly, the final PMC report is expected in June of 
2022. Although contemporaneous approval of a companion diagnostic device is preferable, 
given the circumstances of this application (including rare disease, high mortality, and observed 
clinical effects), I do not believe that approval of tebentafusp should be delayed for about 6 (or 
more) months while waiting for the approval of the device.

## Financial Disclosure

The Applicant’s Position:

Studies IMCgp100-102 and IMCgp100-202 are the two covered clinical studies.  There is 
nothing to declare for financial interest by any investigator.  At the time of conduct, data 
collection and analysis of these studies Immunocore was not public; therefore, there is no 
conflict to disclose.  All financial support for the covered studies were for cost to conduct the 
studies and tracked by Immunocore’s financial function.   
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA notes there may be conflict of interest outside of public trading; however, given that all 
financial support was for cost to conduct the studies, FDA agrees there was no reportable 
conflicts of interest in the conduct of the two studies.  
 
FDA has split the form filled out by the applicant into separate forms, one for each covered 
study.

## Nonclinical Pharmacology/Toxicology

The Applicant’s Position:

Tebentafusp can only recognize human HLA; therefore, all nonclinical toxicology studies were 
conducted in vitro. Human tissue and cell-based in vitro approaches were taken to understand 
potential organ-specific toxicities that may arise in the clinical setting with tebentafusp. These

approaches considered the on-target/off-tumor potential effects, as well as the off-target/off-tumor 
effects (cross-reactivity) of tebentafusp.

Tebentafusp was also investigated in toxicology studies to assess its cross-reactivity with normal 
tissues in a GLP-compliant tissue cross-reactivity study. The ability of tebentafusp to bind to a 
panel of 35 normal human tissues from 3 healthy donors was assessed using 
immunohistochemistry (IHC). Staining with tebentafusp was observed in the membrane and 
cytoplasm of lymphocytes throughout the human tissue panel examined. Similar staining was 
observed with the individual anti-CD3 component of tebentafusp, while no staining was 
observed with the individual TCR component, indicating that this staining was attributable to the 
binding of tebentafusp to CD3. As CD3 is a T lymphocyte marker, this staining was expected. 
No other staining was observed across the panel of tissues tested, indicating no unexpected 
cross-reactivity. It should be noted that the TCR targeting domain of tebentafusp recognizes very 
low target pHLA complexes (>5 pHLA complexes per cell), which are expected to be outside the 
normal range of sensitivity of the IHC method and would therefore inform on cross-reactivity 
above the threshold of detection of IHC only. Overall, the results of this study are consistent with 
published reports of gp100 being specific to melanocytes and melanoma cells, and not in other. 
 
The FDA’s Assessment: 
FDA generally agrees with the Applicant’s position. See FDA’s Assessment in Section 5.5.1.

#### OCP Appendices (Technical documents supporting OCP

The FDA’s Assessment: 
 
Basic characteristics of immunogenicity:

 Anti‐drug antibodies (ADA) positive rate is 28.6% (63/225 patients) in study

IMCgp100-202 and 33.3% (48/144) in study IMCgp100-102.  
 Median ADA onset time was 8 weeks (range: around 1 -30 weeks). 
 ADA positive rate was 14.4% (30/208 patients) at the week 8 landmark in study

IMCgp100-202.  
 Median ADA titer was 8192. There were about 12.6% of patients who developed an

ADA titer >=8192.  
Impact of immunogenicity on PK:

 Clearance increases by 32.9-fold in patients with high titer ADA (defined as

titer>8192). As a consequence, terminal half-life reduced from 6-7 hours to 10-14 
minutes in this subgroup of patients. Relevant labeling of the basic characteristics of 
ADA and impact of immunogenicity on clearance was updated in section 6.2 and 
section 12.3 of the tebentafusp USPI.  
 
Impact of immunogenicity on efficacy:

 An exploratory analysis of effect of ADA on outcomes of tebentafusp was conducted.

For overall survival (OS), hazard ratio for the ADA 8 weeks’ positive subgroup is 
0.65 (95% CI: 0.36- 1.16) and hazard ratio for ADA 8 the weeks’ negative subgroup 
is 0.44 (95% CI: 0.3, 0.64). The immunogenicity positive subgroup did notshow 
significant reduced efficacy compared with the immunogenicity negative subgroup. 
However, the result needs to be interpreted with caution due to the limited number 
of patients (N=30) in the ADA 8 weeks’ positive subgroup. 
 An exploratory analysis of effect of high titer ADA on treatment effect of tebentafusp

was also conducted. For overall survival (OS), hazard ratio for the high titer ADA 8 
weeks’ positive subgroup (titer>=128) is 0.41 (95% CI: 0.35- 1.13) and hazard ratio 
for the ADA 8 weeks’ low titer or negative subgroup is 0.48 (95% CI: 0.33, 0.69). The 
high titer ADA positive subgroup did not show significant reduced efficacy 
compared with the ADA negative or low titer subgroup. However, the result needs 
to be interpreted with caution due to the limited number of patients (N=11) in the 
high titer subgroup.  
 
Please refer to section 19.5.4 for more details.

#### Population PK Analysis

#### 19.5.1.1. The Applicant’s Position:

Population Pharmacokinetic (PK) analysis was conducted across studies IMC-gp100-01, 
IMCgp100-102 and IMCgp100-202 to (1) characterize the PK properties of tebentafusp after IV 
infusion in melanoma patients and (2) to evaluate potential impact of patient demographics and 
clinical covariates on the PK exposure of tebentafusp. A two-compartment model with first-order 
elimination from the central compartment developed in patients with UM and non-UM was used 
to describe the PK profile. Tebentafusp Cmax was achieved immediately after the end of 
intravenous (IV) infusion (median 0.5 hours), with a geometric mean Cmax of 4063 pg/mL for 
Cycle 1 Day 1 (C1D1) (20 mcg dose) and 13040 pg/mL for C1D15 (68 mcg dose). The increase 
in geometric mean PK exposure (Cmax) of tebentafusp was approximately dose proportional 
between the 20 mcg dose administered on C1D1 and the 68 mcg dose administered on C1D15.  
Subsequent weekly doses of 68 mcg from Cycle 2 and beyond indicated no further accumulation 
of Tebentafusp. From the dose escalation data, the observed t1/2 was 6.8 to 7.5 hours.

Estimated glomerular filtration rate (eGFR) and high-titer anti-drug antibodies (ADA) were 
identified as statistically meaningful covariates of Tebentafusp clearance (CL). In the final 
population PK model, estimated tebentafusp CL slightly decreased in patients with moderate 
renal impairment (creatinine clearance [CrCL] ranging 30 to 59 mL/min). However, high 
interpatient variability (78%) was observed and CL values in renally impaired patients were 
essentially within the range observed in patients with normal renal function. No impact on safety 
or efficacy parameters was identified in patients with mild to moderate renal impairment and no 
dose adjustments are recommended. There is no information available in patients with severe 
renal impairment. Estimated CL considerably increased when patient’s generated ADA titers 
greater than 1:8192. However, neither ADA onset or titer magnitude were associated with safety 
or efficacy and thus, monitoring of ADA is not necessary.

Model Structure 
Tebentafusp concentrations were 
log‐transformed for all modeling. 
Base model: 2‐compartment model 
using ADVAN3 TRANS4 with linear 
elimination from central 
compartment with all |CWRES| >4 
outliers excluded was selected as 
the base population 
pharmacokinetic model (Run # 
507) 
Final model: 2‐compartment model 
with first‐order elimination from 
central compartment. Renal 
function and an ADA titer ≥ 8192 
are covariates affecting CL

274 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the

The final PK model was evaluated using prediction corrected VPC (Bergstrand et al, 2011) to 
simulate 1000 replicated VPC datasets. The 95th percentile intervals across replicates were 
compared to corresponding summary statistics derived from observed data for composite VPC 
(Figure 43) and stratified by dose (Figure 44). The model predicted distribution overlap with the 
observed concentration well, indicating that the final PK model characterized the observed PK 
adequately.

Figure 43. Composite Visual Predictive Check of Population PK Model (Log Scale [Run # 
515])

The blue circle represents the observed concentration. The solid and dashed lines represent the median and 2.5th and 
97.5th percentiles of the observations. The shaded red and blue areas represent the 95% CI of the median and 
2.5th and 97.5th percentiles predicted by the model, respectively.

Source: Population Pharmacokinetic Modeling Report and Exposure-Response Analysis for Tebentafusp, Figure 4

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

276 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The final model was developed by incorporating the effect of relevant covariates on key 
structural model parameters of the base model. Covariates were selected based on clinical 
judgment, mechanistic plausibility, and prior knowledge. PK parameter–covariate relationships 
were initially examined graphically. The model with a discrete covariate ADA effect (ADA titer 
≥ 8192) on CL and a continuous covariate of eGFR on CL were concluded to be the final 
covariate model (Run # 515). 
 
Figure 45. Correlation Matrix of Baseline Covariate Assessment-Continuous Covariates

Source: Population Pharmacokinetic Modeling Report and Exposure Response Analysis for Tebentafusp, Appendix 
Figure 5

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

278 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

Demographic covariates did not influence the inter-individual variability of the model based on 
graphical exploration. Therefore, clinical and physiologic covariates of interest, including renal 
function were added to the model in a stepwise fashion. Due to the molecular weight of 
tebentafusp, the effect of estimated glomerular filtration (eGFR) was investigated as a 
continuous covariate on CL. In the forwards addition of covariates, renal function exhibited the 
largest decrease in OFV and AIC.  
 
Figure 47. Impact of Renal Clearance by Renal Functional Status on Exposure After First 
or Third Dose

Source: Analysis based on data “sdtab515”

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

279 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The final model predicted a trend for faster tebentafusp clearance in ADA-positive patients than 
that of ADA-negative patients, but the distributions of IIV of CL overlapped between the 2 
groups. The ADA effect on PK was further evaluated by stratification of patients with maximum 
ADA titers greater than or equal to the median titer of 1:8192.  In this analysis, tebentafusp 
exposure was predicted to decrease in the presence of high ADA titers (≥ 8192) beyond the third 
dose. 
 
Figure 48. Impact of ADA Titer >=8192 on Exposure.

Source: Analysis based on data “sdtab515”

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

280 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

#### 19.5.1.3. The FDA’s Assessment:

The Applicant’s population PK (PPK) model is generally acceptable with minor changes of the 
definition of immunogenicity. FDA’s position is that ADA status should be treated as time‐
varying covariates. Please refer to section 19.5.4 for detail. Impact of ADA Titer >=8192 on 
exposure was re‐estimated and the USPI was updated in section 12.3. The figures (Figure 15, 
Figure 48) visulazing the ADA effect on PK provided by the applicant treated ADA status or titer 
as a fixed factor; therefore, FDA does not agree with the presentation of the data.

Exposure comparison between hepatic impairment patients was requested by IR:

Exposure has been compared in patients with normal hepatic function (n=455) and patients 
with mild hepatic impairment (n=125) as measured by total bilirubin (TB) and aspartate 
aminotransferase (AST) (TB ≤ upper limit of normal (ULN) and AST > ULN or TB > 1 to 1.5x ULN 
and any AST). No clinically significant difference in the pharmacokinetics of tebentafusp were 
identified based on mild hepatic impairment (Figure 49).

Tebentafusp has not been studied in patients with moderate (TB >1.5 to 3x ULN, any AST) to 
severe (TB > 3 to 10x ULN, any AST) hepatic impairment.

Figure 49: Comparison of Clearance between Normal and Mild Hepatic Impairment Patients

Source: Response to FDA request for information received on 2021.12.08.

| Figure 48) visulazing the ADA effect on PK provided by the applicant treated ADA status or titer |
| as a fixed factor; therefore, FDA does not agree with the presentation of the data. |

#### Exposure‐Response Analysis for Efficacy

#### 19.5.2.1. The Applicant’s Position:

Exposure‐response analysis revealed no trends between tebentafusp exposure and key efficacy 
endpoints over the dose range investigated (weekly intravenous [IV] infusion of 5 ng/kg to 68 
mcg of tebentafusp). There was no clinically significant trend between PK exposure and overall 
survival (OS) or maximal change in tumor size from baseline, a surrogate of OS identified in 
Phase 2. There was no trend or association between ADA status and OS.

CR: complete response; CRS: cytokine release syndrome; MR: minor response; n: number; NA: not 
applicable; PD: progressive disease; PR: partial response; SD: stable disease.

a Categorical demographic data is presented as count (% population)

MR was treated as SD in exposure-response analysis. CRS Grade was based on a medical 
adjudication using 2019 ASCTC criteria for grading CRS. The incidence and severity of CRS was 
determined based on AE, concomitant medication, and vital signs data. Therefore, the incidence of 
CRS (based on adjudication by the Sponsor) as an AESI was higher than the incidence of the AE 
term CRS (per investigator).

Source: Population Pharmacokinetic Modeling Report and Exposure-Response Analysis for Tebentafusp, Table 6

Overall, there were no clinically significant trends or associations exhibited between exposure 
and OS. While a slight trend for lower OS in the lowest Cavg quartile was noted in the integrated 
analysis across studies, there was also substantial overlap in OS among the quartiles. The 
apparent trend can be explained by the fact that the lowest Cavg quartile is predominantly 
composed of patients dosed with lower concentrations of tebentafusp from study IMCgp100-01. 
Therefore, monitoring of tebentafusp exposure and dose adjustments are not necessary.

#### Figure 50. Overall Survival by Quartiles of Average Tebentafusp Concentrations

Left Panel: Integrated summary across studies IMCgp100-01, IMCgp100-102 and IMCgp100-202. Right Panel: 
Analysis by individual study. For boxplots, bottom and top halves of each box correspond to first and third quartiles, 
respectively (inter quartile IQR), line inside box is median of the distribution. Upper and lower whiskers extend 
from the hinge to values ≤1.5ꞏIQR from hinge. Outlier data beyond whiskers plotted individually as solid circles. 
Quartile 1 (orange)= 0 to 2592.6 pg/mL, Quartile 2 (green) = 2592.6 to 4217.5 pg/mL, Quartile 3 (blue) = 4217.5 to 
5710.4 pg/mL, Quartile 4 (purple) = 5710.4 to 27005.0 pg/mL. Source: Module 2.7.2, Figure 17
