Figure 51. Kaplan Meier Curve of Quartiles of Tebentafusp Cavg and Overall Survival

Quartiles represent the quartile of average concentration with 68 mcg dose. Quartile 1= 0 to 2592.6 pg/mL, Quartile 
2 = 2592.6 to 4217.5 pg/mL, Quartile 3 = 4217.5 to 5710.4 pg/mL, Quartile 4 = 5710.4 to 27005.0 pg/mL. Numbers 
at risk represent number of individual patients within each quartile of Cavg. 
Source: Module 2.7.2, Figure 18

on Tumor Size by ADA Status

ADA = anti-drug antibody; CR = complete response; PD = progressive disease; PR = partial response; SD = stable 
disease 
Solid lines represent loess line by responder status. Open squares represent ADA negative patients, solid dots 
represent ADA positive patients. Black dots/squares and loess line represent patients with PD. Blue dots/squares 
and loess line represent responders (patients with PR, SD, or CR).

Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

291 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

#### 19.5.2.3. The FDA’s Assessment:

The Applicant’s analysis is reasonable; however, exposure‐response relationships for 
biologic products should be interpreted with caution due to the potential for post‐hoc 
confounding effects.

#### Exposure‐Response Analysis for Safety

#### 19.5.3.1. The Applicant’s Position:

Exposure-response analysis revealed no trends between tebentafusp exposure and key safety 
endpoints over the dose range investigated (weekly intravenous [IV] infusion of 5 ng/kg to 68 
mcg of tebentafusp). There was no association between PK exposure and acute skin reaction, 
rash, hypo/hyper-pigmentation, or hepatoxicity. Cytokine release syndrome (CRS) is known to 
be dose dependent, and there was a trend for lower PK exposure in patients with no CRS. There 
was no trend between PK exposure and interleukin (IL) 6 concentration or either baseline or on-
treatment lymphocyte counts.

#### 19.5.3.2. ER Safety Summary Table [Do not modify the grey cells.]

#### Table 77: ER Safety Summary Table

#### General Information

Goal of ER analysis 
• To evaluate exposure‐response relationship of adverse 
events (eg, skin toxicity, hepatic toxicity, and Cytokine 
Release Syndrome [CRS]) 
• To evaluate exposure‐response of exploratory adverse 
events (eg, rash, hypo/hyper‐pigmentation) 
Study Included 
Due to small number of patients in several dosing 
cohorts and the limited PK sampling beyond cycle 1, the 
PK from studies IMCgp100‐01, IMCgp100‐102 and 
IMCgp100‐202 were combined as an integrated analysis 
to investigate effect of PK on safety.

Overall Clinical Relevance for 
ER 
There was no clinically significant 
trend between PK exposure and 
overall survival (OS) or maximal 
change in tumor size from baseline, 
a surrogate of OS identified in 
Phase 2. Overall, there was no 
clinically significant trend or 
association between ADA status 
and key efficacy endpoints. 
There was no association between 
PK exposure and key on‐treatment 
toxicities including: acute skin 
reactions, rash, hypo/hyper‐
pigmentation or hepatoxicity. CRS is 
known to be dose dependent, and 
there was a trend for lower PK 
exposure in patients with no CRS. 
Labeling Language 
Description 
Acceptability 
[FDA’s comments] 
12.2 Pharmacodynamics 
The proposed 
description 
appears 
reasonable.

(b) (4)

| Overall Clinical Relevance for ER | There was no clinically significant trend between PK exposure and overall survival (OS) or maximal change in tumor size from baseline, a surrogate of OS identified in Phase 2. Overall, there was no clinically significant trend or association between ADA status and key efficacy endpoints. There was no association between PK exposure and key on‐treatment toxicities including: acute skin reactions, rash, hypo/hyper‐ pigmentation or hepatoxicity. CRS is known to be dose dependent, and there was a trend for lower PK exposure in patients with no CRS. |  |  |  |

CR: complete response; CRS: cytokine release syndrome; MR: minor response; n: number; NA: not applicable; PD: 
progressive disease; PR: partial response; SD: stable disease.

a Categorical demographic data is presented as count (% population)

MR was treated as SD in exposure-response analysis. CRS Grade was based on a medical adjudication using 2019 
ASCTC criteria for grading CRS. The incidence and severity of CRS was determined based on AE, concomitant 
medication, and vital signs data. Therefore, the incidence of CRS (based on adjudication by the Sponsor) as an 
AESI was higher than the incidence of the AE term CRS (per investigator).

Source: Population Pharmacokinetic Modeling Report and Exposure-Response Analysis for Tebentafusp, Table 6

Cavg after 1st dose of Tebentafusp 
Cavg after 3rd dose of Tebentafusp

Cavg = average serum concentration; CR = complete response; PD = progressive disease; PR = partial response; SD 
= stable disease

Top Left Panel: Integrated results of effect of average tebentafusp concentration on skin reaction after first dose (20 
mcg). Bottom Left Panel: Integrated results of effect of average tebentafusp concentration on skin reaction after 
first dose stratified by toxicity grade. Top Right Panel: Integrated results of effect of average tebentafusp 
concentration on skin reaction after third dose (68 mcg). Bottom Right Panel: Integrated results of effect of 
average tebentafusp concentration on skin reaction after third dose (68 mcg) stratified by toxicity grade. Toxicity 
severity was based on CTCAE v4.03 criteria.

For boxplots, the bottom and top half of box correspond to the first and third quartiles, respectively (inter quartile 
IQR), while line inside box is median of the distribution. Upper and lower whiskers extend from hinge to values 
≤1.5ꞏIQR from the hinge. Outlier data beyond whiskers are plotted individually as solid circles.

White boxes represent patients with PD; Grey boxes represent patients with PR, SD, or CR.

Patients were classified for CRS based on adjudicated American Society for Transplantation and 
Cellular Therapy (ASTCT) 2019 consensus grading for CRS. A trend was observed for lower 
Cavg after both the first and third dose, and lower Cmax after the third dose in patients who did not 
experience CRS, independent of response status.

310 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

The effect of tebentafusp PK exposure on IL-6 secretion was evaluated by plotting IL-6 
concentrations over the first 48 hours after administration by response status or against the Cmax 
and Cavg values following the first dose (20 mcg). IL-6 levels increased 8 hours post dose, then 
decreased approximately 12 - 24 hours post dose in patients independent of disease status 
(progressive disease, partial response, or stable disease).

The effect of tebentafusp PK exposure on ALC and whether there were differences due to low 
baseline ALC levels (< 109) were evaluated. There was no trend for tebentafusp PK exposure 
(Cavg or Cmax) by baseline ALC stratification (1.0 x 109/L).

Figure 67. Box Plots of Tebentafusp Cavg and Baseline Lymphocyte Count by Responder 
Status

Cavg after third dose of Tebentafusp

CR = complete response; PD = progressive disease; PR = partial response; SD = stable disease  
For the boxplots, the bottom and top half of the box correspond to the first and third quartiles, respectively (inter 
quartile IQR), while the line inside in the box is the median of the distribution. The upper and lower whiskers 
extend from the hinge to the values no further than 1.5ꞏIQR from the hinge. Outlier data beyond whiskers are 
plotted individually as solid circles.

19.5.3.3. The FDA’s Assessment: 
The Applicant’s analyses were reasonable; however, exposure‐response relationships for 
biologic products should be interpreted with caution due to the potential for post‐hoc 
confounding effects.

#### FDA’s Overall Independent Assessment

Key Review Questions:  
1. What are the basic characteristics of tebentafusp immunogenicity?

The ADA positive rate was 28.6% (63/225 patients) in pivotal study IMCgp100-202 and 
33.3% (48/144) in study IMCgp100-102. The ADA positive rate was 4% (3/78) in early-
stage trial IMCgp100-01.

The time to median ADA onset was 8 weeks with a range from 1 -30 weeks (Figure 68).

#### Figure 68: Histogram of anti‐drug antibody onset time (weeks)

Source: Reviewer’s independent analysis. Red line is the median onset time (8 weeks) 
 
Tebentafusp ADA titer time course was shown in Figure 69 stratified by study and different 
dose levels.

#### subgroups:

Source: Clinical Pharm Team Reviewer’s Independent Analysis.  
 
Population PK Analysis:  
Since ADA titer is a time-varying covariate, FDA requested the applicant to re-define 
MAXTITFL as follows:

‐ 
When “ADATITER” >=8129, “MAXTITFL” was defined as 1.  
‐ 
Otherwise “MAXTITFL” was defined as “.” 
With the new dataset “nonmen200.csv” and the final structure model (run 515), the newly 
estimated high titer ADA (>8192) increased tebentafusp clearance 32.9-fold. And this value 
was updated in section 12.3 of the tebentafusp USPI.  
 
3. What is the impact of tebentafusp immunogenicity on efficacy?  
An exploratory analysis of the effect of ADA on treatment outcomes of tebentafusp was 
conducted (Figure 71: left). Patients in both the tebentafusp arm and the control arm who 
had an event or were censored less than 8 weeks were removed. The new ADA status 
grouped based on ADA status at 8 weeks were listed as follows:

NDA/BLA Multi‐disciplinary Review and Evaluation BLA 761228 
Kimmtrak (tebentafusp)

318 
Version date: January 2020 (ALL NDA/ BLA reviews) 
 
Disclaimer: In this document, the sections labeled as “Data” and “The Applicant’s Position” are completed by the 
Applicant and do not necessarily reflect the positions of the FDA.

ADA 8 weeks status 
N (%)

ADA+ 8 weeks 
30/208 (14.4%)

ADA- 8 weeks 
178/208 (85.6%)

Based on cox regression analysis, for overall survival (OS), the hazard ratio for the ADA 8 
weeks’ positive subgroup is 0.65 (95% CI: 0.36- 1.16) and hazard ratio for the ADA 8 
weeks’ negative subgroup is 0.44 (95% CI: 0.3, 0.64) (Table 79). The ADA positive 
subgroup did not show significant reduced efficacy compared with the ADA negative 
subgroup. However, these results need to be interpreted with caution due to the limited 
number of patients (N=30) in the ADA 8 weeks’ positive subgroup. 
 
To explore the impact of high titer ADA on efficacy, an exploratory analysis of the effect of 
high titer ADA on treatment outcomes of tebentafusp was conducted (Figure 71, right). 
Based on cox regression model, for overall survival (OS), the hazard ratio for high titer ADA 
8 weeks’ positive subgroup (titer>=128) is 0.41 (95% CI: 0.35- 1.13) and hazard ratio for 
ADA 8 weeks’ low titer or negative subgroup is 0.48 (95% CI: 0.33, 0.69) (Table 79). The 
cut-off of titer 128 was the median ADA titer at week 8. The high titer ADA positive 
subgroup did not show significant reduced efficacy compared with the ADA negative or low 
titer subgroup. However, these results need to be interpreted with caution due to the 
limited number of patients (N=11) in the high titer subgroup.

left figure and titer >=128 in the right figure). Green line represents ADA 8 weeks negative patients (overall 
negative in the left figure and titer<128 in the right figure). Gray line represents control group.

#### Summary of Bioanalytical Method

The Meso Scale Discovery (MSD) method was used to determine tebentafusp in human 
serumusing HLA‐A2 antigen capture in Study IMCgp100‐01, Study IMCgp100‐102 and 
IMCgp100‐202. This method employs an indirect sandwich immunoassay format, with 
biotinylated HLA‐A2 gp100 antigen used to capture the tebentafusp monoclonal TCR. After 
incubation with analyte, a rabbit anti‐gp100 TCR antibody step is used followed by detection 
with a SULFO‐TAG conjugated goat anti‐rabbit antibody. The lower limit of quantification 
(LLOQ) of the method is 25 pg/mL and the upper limit of quantification (ULOQ) is 5,000 pg/mL. 
This method was developed and validated at 
. 
 
Analytical Method 
/007/V10 was validated over the concentration range 25 to 5,000 pg/mL 
in undiluted serum samples. The concentration levels of tebentafusp (Lot 00644, 0.5 mg/mL 
concentration) were as follows: 25 (LLOQ), 125 (Low), 600 (Medium), 3,200 (High), 5,000 
(ULOQ) and 50,000 (dilution) pg/mL. The dilution quality control was diluted 100‐fold with 
control human serum prior to analysis and the data confirmed linearity of dilution into the 
working range of the assay with up to 100‐fold dilution in serum. 
 
The intra‐batch precision was less than or equal to 14.0% and the intra‐run bias was 
between ‐13.6% and 3.0%. The inter‐batch precision was less than or equal to 13.7% and the 
inter‐batch bias was between ‐9.4% and 5.6%. The total error of the method was less than, or 
equal to 21.1% for the intra‐batch data and less than or equal to 21.3% for the inter‐batch data. 
The target LLOQ in this validation was 25 pg/mL; precision and bias at this level were found to 
be acceptable. 
 
The long‐term stability of tebentafusp (Lot 00644, 0.5 mg/mL concentration) when spiked into 
human serum and stored at ‐80°C was successfully assessed and established using the analytical 
method previously validated at YBS. Stability was assessed after approximately 6, 12, and 24 
months. In addition, the stability of tebentafusp in working solution (assay buffer) when stored 
at ‐80°C was investigated after approximately 6 and 12 months of storage in polypropylene 
containers. Tebentafusp was found to be stable in human serum stored at ‐80°C for up to 24 
months and in working solution when stored at ‐80°C for up to 373 days.

(b) (4)
